The noble experience of the virtuous handy Warke of surgeri / practysyd
compiled by the most expert master Iherome of Bruynswyke / borne in
Straesborowe in Almayne / ye which hath it first proved / and trewly found by
his awne daily exercysynge. Item there after he hath authorysed and done it to
understand thrugh the true sentences of the old doctors and masters very
expert in the science of Surgery / As Galienus / Ipocras / Auicenna / Gwydo /
Haly abbas / Lancfrancus of mylen / Iamericus / Rogerius / Albucasis /
Placetinus / Brunus / Gwilhelmus de saliceto / by many other masters whose
names be written in this same book. Here also shall ye find for to cure heal
all wounded mebres / and other swellynges. Item if ye find any names of herbs
or of other things whereof ye have no knowledge / yt shall ye know plainly by
the potecarys. Item Here shall you find also for to make salves / plasters /
powders / oils / and drynkes for wounds. Item whosoever desires of this science
ye plain knowledge let him oftentimes rede this book / and than he shall get
perfyte understanding of the noble surgery.







The Prologe of the noble hand work of Surgery.
TO ye laud of our sauyour Christ Ihesu. the honour of his blessyd moder our
lady saint mary. and all the holy copa ny of heuyn. for the help of mankynde /
this book is translated out of duche in to englis^he And for ye love comfort
of all them that entende to study the noble art of Chyrur gia / ye which is
called the handyworke of Surgery / very vtyle and profytable to al that entende
to occupy this noble sciens ye herein is openly expressed and showed / how it
shall be practysed used / For many one is therein very ignorant yt will meddle there
with / which never laboured nor never sa point of ye beginning or ending
thereof / wherefore it is often times senc and daily chances in small towns /
borowghs / villages / that lyefarre from any good cite or great town ye
dyuerie people hurt or diseased for lack of conynge men / be taken in hand of
them yt be barbers or young masters to whom this sciens was never disclosed /
not thinking on the words of the old lernydmen that say / It is not well
possible to man that he should bring well to a good end yt thing which he
never or hath but little scene. Thus ye yonge studyntys / masters / ieruautes
of barbers and surgyens that entende this noble art conynge / behold / ouerse
/ and rede with diligence this little book that I Iheronims Bruynswyke borne in
Straesborowgh / out of the lyne of Salerne / has with great labour copyled /
set / gadered together to your behoof great profyt this little volume /
thinking on many noble auctours in divers bokys / which playuly doth specesy
/ Iursyd be those that god hath with conynge endowed to the health / succour /
help of mankynde / will not occupy it. But vlessyd be they that among his
euyn crysten will liberally sheme and mynistre such gifts of grace as god
has endewyd him with for the preserua cyon of man. Wherefore my frendys think
yt ye may now for a little money have great learning conynge to your honour
profit / the which herafter ye might fortune not to get for ten times so
much gold as it should cost you now.

Oy yonge brgynnynge surgyens unclose yourerys w all your diligence and mark
well the words of the great masters which command you when ye be called or
desired to any pacyent or diseased parsone / that if the dyseas fall to your
conynge to ponderous / that ye be not fully parfyte / than be not ashame but
quicly get another discrete surgyen or ^mayndesyrynge them that they will
help ^ sell you in yt besynes at your need * sor yo^ honesty lyath in that
cure / also the great coforte of your paeyet so dy^eased. Ey^st ye learn by
chance / that thing that ye seldon or never have scene before. Serodarily / if
ought in your hands happen to misfortune * that ye other may quycly than
amend it. Thyrdly / that the wounded parson have ye less grudge or mystrust
in you. Fourthly / When the cure hath good speed / tha be ye parttaker of al the
honour thereof / if yt misfortune fall between your handys / than be they boude
every man to bear the charge of your hinder and losses / which were to much
for you alone.

Fyftly / for this wise dede ye be praised of all them that be discrete or
learned men yt speak of you / which say / he desires to learn / and will not
that any man should be by him neglygently spylt or peryshed. and thus mayye
come to yone poncpose with honesty and pleasure / which else might turn to
yourgrete shame dysplesure.

Also ye may consydere that two may better amend a fawte tha one / for no
only workman can well parceyue the fawtys of his own work alone till he hath
very lunge wrought upon it / or else ne'er hand fynyshte hit / and than is it
sometime evil ipostyble to be mendyd / but pryncypally in many operacyons
belonging to surgery / Therefore when ye go two or more about the pacyent / take
heed that ye make no dyscorde* In like wise when any of you be present alone
with your pacyent / blame ^at the other that is absent / nor dyffame him not
But what ye have to say withe each other let that be secrete within your self
for grewynge of your pacyente / for it might turn him to great payne
hyndraunce in his dyseas through your dyscoforte. The one shall follow the
others counsel and (...) shall ^de nothing from each other that ye shall
think profytable beho^ for your pacyent or seek body / for (...) turn you to
shame / and him to great payne. Also ye ought not only to be ^pert in surgery
but also in astronomy or philosophy / wher^ore ye shall diligently study often
rede such things as for you in this matter or scyens shall be vtylle profytable
whereby ye shall have parfytte vnderstondynge knowledge of your noble science
that ye do enterprise / ye shall for no gold nor silver take in hand ye
thing that ye think is incurable / or not likely to be cured / for sauyge of
your goodname Also ye shall not praise yourself / nor blame none other. Item
ye shall also counforte your pacyent how so ever it be with him but to his good
frendys ye shall show the truth give them parsyte knowledge of his dyseas.
Also ye should know under stoned parfytly your Anathomia / which is the
gaderynge and also ye dysmebrynge of the lymmes of ye body / becauseye should
preserve man for the iopardy of death / if it need required that ye should cut
him in any place would doing to him any scathe and to yourselffe an
everlasting / shame / and great dishonesty.

AFter these chaptours folowethe the Antidotharius / in the which thou may
learn how thou shalt make many divers noble plasters / salves / powders / oils
/ and wound drynkes / the which be very necessary and behooveful / vtyll /
profytable for every surgyon therein to be expert / and ready at all times of
need:

Here begins the handworke of Anothomia in general / of ye members / skin
flesh / veins / senowys / and bonys.


The Anothomia in general
THe skin is a covering of the hole vnyuersall body woven out of the veins
senewes / made for the defence of ye wits of man / and ye same skin is
twain indyfferet. The one doth cover the uttermost membre / that is named the
very skin / The other covers the innermost part of the membrys and it is
named panniculus / or pannycle / that is as a flece / like as by the felles or
chambres of the brain / and pyrocraneum is ye thyn flece above the braynpanne
/ and ye panycle of the rybbes is named Pleura and Siphac / and the pannycle of
the heart and other. c. Here after follows the fatnesses / some is within the
skin that is na / med greece / some is within by ye belly about the kydneys and
that is named talowe

Tha comes the flesh which be in. iij. manners / some is pure simple flesh
/ as is only the yard and the gomys of the teeth / that other is as carnel^ys
/ like the flesh of the coddys of the breast / the iij. is copre hendynge
almost overall the hole body is named caroplena lacertis. Than begins the
synewes to take their effect of the brains of the mary of the back / After
yt the veins takes their effect of the liver and of ye heart. Than follows
the bonys of ye body / and of them be in nobre. CC. xlviij. beside ye small
bonys that be called ossa cisanina and the bone laud / whereon ye tongue is
fowndyd. The nails be made on the uttermost part of ye mebres because they
should ye stronghyer grype and hold all manner of things. The hear is ordained
for fayrnes and to purifye the manyfolde partis of the body.

The anothomia of the composyde membris. Ca. ij.
HEre begins of the heed / and pryncypally of the brains / of the pan^ that
kepeth ye brains together / for that is ye place dwelling of ye reasonable
soul and all that is heard is namyd the (...) of the heed / and therein be ye
vnderstadynge members / that is in the highest part of man / the quantyte of
the brains of mankynde is much more tha it is of any other reature /
considering the strength of ma agyanst the gretnes of other dome creatures.
The {per}ties of this pane be. x. or. xj. first without is the hear / than ye
skin / than flesh of lacertes / than a gross pannycle or flece / than the
pan / than ^in be ij. small fleces named dura matter / and pia matter / than
the substance of the brains / and after the substance of ye brains is again
pia matter / and after that / lyath that marvelous net and is named Rethe
mirabile / tha above that is named the foudacion of the brains / out of the
which the senewes take their beginning. That panicle that is named of Galien^
pericraneum doth covers all the hole pan / is somewhat like to senewes /
and grows of dura matter / of her is strongly bownde senewes veins / after
this is craneu found and is named the pan of the heed / and that is not a
hole bone / but. vii. bonys ordained to each other / and that is because of
this / yfone by fortune were hurt in ye one bone / yt the other shulde not be
perysshed / and they be gadered together like a seem or a thing like the teeth
of. ij. saws joined in one / to thentent that the some of the heed should have
an yssewe. The first bone of the pan is named coronale going from the
myddest orbitarum to the ^whart joints of the pan / and therein be hoolys of
ye iyen and the out berynge of the nose / depart through a little bone like a
cock^s comb / but in ye women it is often founden that the coronale is divided
ouertwhart in the myddest of the forheed. The. ij. bone is of ye hinder part /
and namyd occipiciale / is closyd through a joint coming over thwarte ilyke
manner of this figure / is harde / thrugh persed / where as Nucha which is the
mary yt comith in / through ye rydge bone or chyne to ye end of the back The.
iij.. iiij. bone be in the myddys of syd^am be namyd Parietales / be divided
through a joint by ye length of ye pane coming to the bonys of ye eerys / they
be iiij. square. The. v. ye syxt bone be called Petrosa for their hardness /
also they be namyd Medosa / they be gaderyd with ye bonys by ye sides where as the
holys of ye erys the clensynge of the breast be in / be led toward ye commyssure
of the bone la^de to ye myddys of the temple bonys. The. vij. is yt fundament
bone namyd Basillare / is facyoned like a cradyll / and supports all the for
said bonys above the rose of the ^o^th / thus ye shall understand yt there be
vi^. manner of bonys in the pot of the heed which is all the vpperparte. thus
is to be vnderstade that therbe. vij. boys that keep the brains in. / yet
there be other bonys yt be no pryncypallys as ye bone c^yste which deuydeth the
nose thryllys between the coronall bone / there be other bonys that be namyd
Paria belonging to the face / and not to the pan / also there be crokyd bonys
under the bone of the eerys where as musculus is plated in / which opyn ye Jawe
bonys. The lymmys that in the inner part of the heed be holden we can not
show parfytely with ye Iye nor kno^ therefore we shall deuyde ye (...) pan
with a saw roundabou^ heed / and when they lift up ye (...) per part from the
neder part / ye first that follows is dura matter pia matter / and be ij.
s^nowlyke panycles / wyndynge about keeping in the holl substa^ce of the brayn
/ of dura matter grows through the comissures of ye pane pericraneu / of pia
matter is genyn ye fode of the brains / of he^ comes veins vain strigys fro
withinforth through ye holys of the undermost bonys / without forth through ye
comys^res of ye uppermost bonys.

The knowledge of ye. x. wits. v. interyall. and. v. comune wits. as it
scewyd i ye picture of the heed. (...).

AFter pia matter follows ye substance of the brain / and is soft whyt / and
round of figure when the addycyons be taken from her The brain hath. iij.
cellys or chambers somewhat lunge / and each celle hath. ij. partis / and in
every part is a part of our understanding / In the first celle is our common
wyttis / as it is expressly scene in this figure of ye heed / these be they
Saying in ye iyen / Smelling in ye nose / Tastynge in ye tongue / Hearing in ye
ears / Fylynge overall ye body. In the second is the ymagynacyon / in the.
iij. is wynynge reason / in ye. iiij. is remebrauce memory / there be ways from
the one to ye other / to the^tent that ye spirytis may have their fre course
from one to another / and in the first celle be more addycyons wherein is closyd
our smelling / thereof grows. ij. couples of synowes / they be led to the
iyes / to the erys / to the tongue / to the stomach / to other lymes through
holys closyd with panycles. By the second cell^ mark the place yt is namyd
lacuma / vermiformis / anchaformis / and the cornell flesh. And under ye
panycle is rethe mirabile yt only is woven with vaynst^ingis coming from the
heart / in the which is coprehendyd under fonge ye quick understanding
spiritys. Fynally / mark how that nucha or that rydge bone mary grows of the
last part of the brain / whereof pryncypally all our meuynge vnderstadynge
synowys have there first original begynyng / thus is ye A^nothomia of ye brayn
pane openly know may suffer many wouder hurtis / but ye ne^er ye brayn ye
worse. and in ye workynge of the heed if need require you shalt cut ye same
flesh of the heed according as ye here gothe which way so ever it be.

The anothomia of the face. ca. iij.
THe {per}tys of ye face be these / ye forheed browys / iyes / eerys / templis
/ chekys / mowth / iawys / with her teeth. The forheed hath but ye skyne upon ye
musculy / or flesh called lacerte / for ye bone yt is under it is of the
coronall bone / and is raised toward ye upper table like a dowble bone makes
ye form of ye brows. The brows be made for beauty / set above ye iyen with
here for to defend them / ye cuttynge yt is done to them must go after ye
length of the body / not ye way yt ye frounces go. The iye be ye instrumetis of
ye sight / be ordained a part in ye coronall bone by ye bonis of ye temple / ye
iye be made of. vij. cotys. iiij. humours / The first cote is without forth is
namyd / coiunctiua alba / and grossa / that roneth about the iye / and grows
of the panycle that covers ye brayn pane / after this there be. iij.
material circles yt run about the iye / and because they be so differet of
colours they be called yride or rain bowys / there be. iij. of these cotys yt
comes from the side of ye brains /. iij. from the utter parties / ye first
cote grows of dura matter / ye inner part thereof is named scly^otica / ye
uttermost part is named cornea The other cote grows of pia mr. / ye iner
part thereof is named secudina / the utter most thereof is named v^ea / hath the
hole of the ball of the iye. The third grows of the senowe optico / the
inner part thereof is named retina / and the uttermost thereof upon the bright
crystallyn is named Aranea / to this be. iiij. princypall moystours The first
moystour is named cristallyna / and it is set in the myddis of the iyen / and
is of colour like crystal / and is facyoned like a hayll stone / wherein the
sight is pricypally foudyd / after yt toward ye braynis is vitreous humour
which holds circuyteth from behind ye crystallyn humour these twain be
wode about with one panycle in ye senewe optico / after yt from before is the
humour albugyneus yt is whytysshe / and is conclud^d between ^he (...) be before
said the web yt grows of pia matter: G^enus alegith another moystours is in
ye region of the balle of the iye / and that is clear of a heuenly element
colour and is hole fomys^he or scomye / and this is the coposyssyon of the iye
in him self. The iye has cartilag^ above under which we name the iye lyddis
with here that close from above with one musclus / opyn with twhart musclus. The
nose hath flesshy / ^onye / and grystly partis / the flesshy {per}te hath a
skyne and. ij. musclus by each other and the bony part hath. ij. tryangle bonis
/ which corners comes on the nose shyftynge them on the one side along ye
nose / coming down to ye cheke / the grystyll {per}te is of two manners / the
one is without that ^acyneth the utter part of the nose / and ye other
deuydeth the ynner part of the nose thryllys. And the. ij. holys of ye nose
ascend upward to ye bonys colatorij / be addyd to mamillares cerebri / where
as ye smelling hath his begynynge / these go backward down to the rowfe of the
mowth behind vuula / through which holys is drawyn the brethynge vapour / both
out and in / the superfluyte of the brains puryfyde. The eeris be grystly upon
ye petrosu bone ordained for to here / to the which yt come otwahrt holys unto
the ^enewes of ye brains where the heerynge is / under the eerys is flesh
like carnellis that makes the puryfienge of ye brains / by the which goothe.
ij. veins yt convey ye spermatyke or seedly matter or substance down to the
ballockis. The temples / leyres / chek^ / be the parties of the sydys of the
face / and have in them much musclus flesh: first there be. vij. meuyng the
chekys and the upper lyppys / after these be. xij. that meue the undermost Jawe
bone / some opening it that come from beside the erys / and some closing it /
and they come from above beside ye teples bonys / if they bewoudyd / it is
great jeopardy. Though it seem yt there be but ij. bonis gadered to gender above
the nose / yet some say there be nyne.:* There be. v. partis of ye mouth / ye
lyppys teeth / tongue / rowfe / and vuula / ye which is a little deem hanging
in ye throat like the spin. The teeth of the nature of the bonys / of them
be. xxxij. that is in every cheke ^one or Jawe xvi. of the which ij. be named
duales. ij. quadrupli. ij. canini* ij. caysales. iij. molares. have rotis
festenyd in the Jawbonys / some one rote / some ij. some more. The toge is a
soft flesshy / spongy part / made of many seynowes / stryngys / veins /
pricypally ordained for the spece favourable taste / to rule the mete in the
mouth. Under ye tongue is a cornell flesh / where as. ij. holys like mouths
be in / where the spetyll comes out of: Behind the tongue is the Jawflesshe by
(...) rowf of ye mouth with knotys like an ^ and between those. ii. hangs
vuula (...) saith / is ordained to take the air and to make it apt. The upper
{per}te of ye mouth is named the rowf / is covered with a panycle / takes his
beginning on the forner part of ye maw or stomach.

Of the neck / and back bone. Ca. iiij.
TWo parts be in the neck / some do holden / some be holden / The holding
parts be these / shynne flesh / muscl^ stryngys / and bonys. The {per}tes
that be holdyn be these. the throat bolle or trachea / ^sophagus or meri / that
is where the mete gothe through Epiglotu or gula / veins and strings / and a
part of nucha. First is trachea arteria / that is a way of the brethe or ayr^
coming frome the longues to the throat which is gaderyd bound to the side of
merry with a strong soft panycle / after the throat on the spondyles is merry /
or ysophag{is} / is a way of the descedyng of our sode / gothe from the throat
to dyafragma is made out of. ii. cotys. the innermost is festyned with ye
skin of the mouth / and the uttermost cote is festyned to the panicle of the
belly is fleshye / on these. ii. ways on the side of the mouth is Gula or
Epiglotus / is a grystly part made for the voce / is the place of the
swelowynge down.:. Here after follows ye dowble senowes to the stomach / and
to the lymmes descendynge / again ascendynge upward by Epyglot{is}. After
these be great veins and strings namyd Guidegi / or Apopleti / or subetales.
The divided {per}tes go upward through the sides or the neck unto ye highest
parts / the cuttynge of these be very ieo{per}dus. Spodyle or rydge bone is al
through percyd or boryd / where as Nucha or back mary gothe through / there as
ye senowes in the side gothe up down / the back is it that gothe from ye heed
to the romp bone out of many strong spondyles following each other for the
defence of the back mary which be. xxx. in nobre. vii. in the neck.. xii. by
the should{er}s. v. by the lymmys above the hyppys. after the bone called the
holy bone / there be. iiii. In the neck be. vii. stodyles through ye which
gothe. vii. cowpies of senowes from that part of Nucha that gothe throught it
/ the which bear me uyng to the shulders / armies / some places of the heed
neck Thus do as before is said in the neck / work by ye length for it is
the right way of al ye {per}tes in ye neck.

Of the shulders / armies / and the great hands. Ca. v.
Descending from ye neck doth follow a graet rysynge like a hill / and on the
highest part thereof the shulders be platyd / and yt should{er} bonys be twain
First behid is one broad and thyme on the back party / on yt side of the
ioyntys it is somewhat lunge roude like a haft with. iii. edgys / the first is
holowe / the other above crooked sharpe like ye bill of a crane. That other bone
is named Os furfale / or the forked bone / and is roude festyned in a holownes
in ye upper part of the breast / hath. ii. brauches like a fork / the one
gothe to the one shoulder / the other gothe to the other shoulder / byndyth the.
ii. sharpe crokydendys / and is a hole deffence preserving of all the
should{er} wyntys. The part under the ioyntys of the arm pyttys is made of
cornell flesh / wherein is showed the purging of the heart Galien{is} deuydeth
the arm in. iii. great parties / the first part is a above ye oxcellys or arm
pyttys. the other part is namyde the little arm / the third ye little hade.
The stryngys opyne senowys that be found in the arm coming to the oxcellys
there be deuydyd in twain. The one goth on the highest of the armies / that other
part to the undermost part of the armies.. The veins that ascend be divided
in branches / the one goth up behind the should{er}s to the heed / the other
descendyth is yet divided in twain other branches / where of the one brauche
is divided through the arm on the utter side in divers places / is named funis
brachii / which is the rope of the arm. The other brauche comes up through
the upper part of the arm and is opened showed through ye bendynge of ye
elbow / is namyd Cephalica or the chef vain. From thens it comes for the on
the hand between ye thombe the fore finger / and is namyd cephalica ocularis.
The other veins frome the oxcellis that come to the under part of the arm
show them self in ye bought of ye arm / and is namyd basilica which is the
vain of the liver / from thens it descendyth down between ye gold finger and
the little finger / and is namyd saluatella / when the ii. fornamyd vaynys be
in the bought of the arm / than is there another vain scene between them both
/ and is namyd mediana corporalis / and thus there be in the arm. v. great
veins / and so many strings / the which be very ieopardus to stanch if
they were woundyd or cut. Of Nucha through ye spondiles of the neck descendynge
to every arm. iiii. pryncypall senowes / that meue and stere the aduitory or
little arm / and out of it comes. v. senowes into the hand that meue the
fyngers / and they show the self openly on the three fyngers towards the
ioyntys / which is dangerous to be wooded. In ye arms be great stryngys
stryngys the come from the bonys going through ye ioyntys / and keep them
joined / the which were very ieopardus to be cut. The bone namyd vlna or
adiutoriu / is a great bone full of mary / roude at both endys / but above it
hath but one roudnes / and beneth it hath. ii. the uppermost goth into the
holowe of ye gabone / makes the joint of the sholders / and the nether end
which hath. ii. roudnes is divided in. ii. and goth into ye holownes of the.
ii. bonys that be namyd focilium / and they make the ioyntys of the elbows
where as the little arm begyneth / in which little arm be ii. focill bonys /
that be namyd ossa focilia / and the grettest is benethe / and that goth
toward ye little finger / show a rownde knot outward / the small focille
bone goth above from the bought of the arm to the hand toward the thombe /
and in both ye upper part of these. ii. bonys be pyttes / or holys by ye
elbow / receive the roundness namyd graduales / of the bone called aduitorii /
by the handys they have pyttys also / which receive the roundne of ye ioyntys
of the hand / and be festenyd just unto the bonys of ye hand making ye
ioyntys / the which ioyntys be. iii. hepys of bonys / and ye uppermost be
gadered with a round nes in the pyttes of the nethermost. In the first hepe be.
iii. bonys / for the addycion of focilles kepeth above the place of a bone. In
the second hepe be. iiii. bonys / there above is a little box wherein is
festenyd ye first bone of the thombe. The bonys of the ii. fornamyd hepys be
short. The first hepe is namyd rafeta / or corp{is}. The other hepe is named
Pectenor Metacorpus.. In the iii. hepe be. iiii. bonys longer than the first In
every finger be. iii. bonys / and the fyngers be in nombre. v. therefore there
be xv. bonys in the fyngers. And in the (...) xi. ii. in the little arm. i. in
the upper (...) And thus there be in the hole arm and hade xxix. bonys. and
these must be cut for to becurydall lunge ways / like as the sacerres and
musclus gothe..

The Anothomie of the breast and his parties a mebres Ca. vi.:.
THe parties in the breast be some holden some that be hold The pappys or brestys
be made as it were a cornelly whyt flesh like a sponge / made with veins /
stryngys / and senowes / and there fore they have a festenynge of the liver of
the heart. The lacertes or musclus be many divers some with the skin named
Dyafragma / some do be lunge only to the breast / some to ye rybbes / some to the
back. Therbe. iii. manners of bonys in the breast. In the first part be. vii.
bonys namyd ossa thoracis Thereby on the side of gula is receyuyd the holowes of
Fircula / under fircula by the ^roppe of the maw or stomach is a grystly
addytamente namyd Cusifornu. On the hinder part be. xii. spondiles where as
nucha passes through / whereof wax or grow. xii. cowple of senowes / ye
which bring sterynge and me nynge to ye musclus or flesh of that part On
every side be. xii. rybbes. vii. ryghtewys rybbes / v. mendosa rybbes or faint
rybbes be cause they be not hole as ye other ryghtwys rybbes ^e. For to do the
Anothomia well of the lymmes that be holden ye must cut the breast towardys the
lyde / put away the first part for mediastum / than may ye inner part be scene
/ of ye which the heart is the first in the myddest of the breast / descendynge
a little toward ye left side / for the place of the liver / and to thentent
that it should give rome or place to ye stryngys. The form or shape of the
heart is like a pine apple / for the point of ye heart gothe toward the neder
lymmys or membrys of the body / the breed of the which is ye root gothe
vpwardys. The substance of the heart is harde having on every side a vetrycle
or holownes / and in ye myddyst a pytt as Galien{is} saith / in which is
consumed the gross fedynge blode that comes from the liver / and is made pure
/ is sent by the veins throughout all the parties of the body. First to the
brains / there it conceives another nature and becomes animalis or
vnderstadinge / to the liver where as it becomes natural fedynge / to the
stones or coddys for generation / so forth to all other membrys or lymmes /
makes them quycke or gives them lyf. The heart is an instrument of al powers
and might of the body / a fulcome bond or festener of ye soul / in it be.
ii. orificias or mowthes and through the right orifice roneth a brauche of ye
ascendynge veins / bringing up the blode frome the liver / descendith frome
thens downward again to vena arterialis for to fed ye longues. Of the lift
orifice gothe ye betynge vain / namyd vena pulsatilis / whereof one part gothe
to ye longues / and it is namyd vena venalis / berynge the vapours capinosos to
the logues / and ledynge the air in / for to cole the hart with all / upon
this orifice be. iii. panycles or skynes opynyng and closing / the passage of
ye blode. By this orifice be. ii. little eerys joined to the heart / where as
the air or breath goth out and in toward the longues. Also there is a little
grystell bone in it for to strength the heart with. The heart is coueryd with a
strong panicle namyd precordiu / where as the senowes come to / be boude with ye
longues festenyd / and subportynge through mediastinu. Upon ye heart comes ye
longues fleing wauynge for to cole it / whose substance is spongye / whyt soft
/ in yt which be. iii. holownessis.. The first is ye veins which grow out
of ye right ventrycle of the heart / the vain that grows out of the lift
ventrycle / the brauches yt comes from the throthe bring wind or breath to ye
heart. The longues hath. v. lobos or feders. iii. in the right side / and. ii.
in those ft side. Behind the longues / after the. v. spondyle goth merry / ye
vain tracea ascedynge / both these pass through dyafragma. Also there pass
through it matter adorthi that doth ascend fro the heart / all these with the
vein Trachea make a hepe fyllyd with panycles and strong bondys / with
caruelly flesh to gula. After this be in the breast. iii. panycles. First the
panycle that fro within doth couere the rybbys named Pleura. The other is
mediastinu / departyth the hole carkes in both sides. The third is dyafragma
/ and yt divides ye spyrytuall lymmys or mebrys from ye fedynge mebrys / and
is made out of pleura and syphac / of the short panycle that growyth of the
senowes between ye spondyles is most by ye rybbes / whose operation is for to
draw the air to her / for to withdryue ye superfluyte as Galien{is}
testyfyeth.

Of ye belly his mebrys. Ca. vii.
Merry is ye crop of ye neck going inwardly thrugh ye neck / till yt he
makyth a hole through dyafragma / where un to he is fast bound / dyafragma goth
into ye last {per}te of ye breast there as ye mouth of the maw or stomach
doth sprede him. The work of the stomach is dysgestyon / for it hath ye liver
on the right side / warning herself with the lobys or lymmes / ye mist thwart
on ye lift side with her fat veins for to drive away melacoly or heuynes / for
to lyghte releue ye appetite. Above it is (...) gyuyng her quyknes unto ye
brains lo^ have ye vndstadyng of feeling. Also it hath of ye back {per}te ye
senowes namyd chylym adorthi / where as it is bound with / unto ye spodiles of yt
kydnes. Unto ye vndmost mouth of ye stomach begyneth the guttys / and they be in
nobre. vi. ye first is namyd duodenu. for he is xii. inches loge. and is also
namyd portenare{is} / for he is ye vndmost {per}^e of ye stomach / like as meri
is up{per}most. The. ii. is ylio / is loge small / is woude up by ye back by
ye lyskes The. iii. is ieiuniu / for he is ever empty / because he is so nygh
the gall / there come to hi ye small veins mise raice / he receives ye colera
yt comes between hi portenariu. The. iiii. is cec{is} or sacc{is} / is ye
blind gut / or second maw or moke / is about ye length of a shaftmet / hath.
i. orificiu to receive ye hole fylthynes yt comes of ye first dysgestyo of ye
bowels. The. v. is namyd Colon / is gross fullof holownes / where as ye
fyshynes receives her form. The. vi. is namyd Longaon / and that is the ars
gut. The Liver is a place an organ of the second dysgest yo engendryng blode
set in the right side under the short rybbes / and is formed like a moan /
hath. v. little panys in the manner of a hade / wherewith passes above the
stomach. The Liver with her panycle is boude on Dyafragma with the back /
stomach / gut / and hath collygacyo with the heart / kydney / coddys / with
all mebrys Her substance is redflesshy like blode that is stollydor ron / is
full of synewes. Of the holownes of the liver comes a vain named the gate /
is divided in many small veins that be namyd miseraice / yt be platyd in ye
stomach / in the guttys draw out all the moisture of the vain Chyli / is
divided with her rotys through all ye liver / and of the hill of the liver
comes the vain Chylis / draws from the liver all the blode that is in it
engendered / beryn ge that blode for to fed ye hole body. In the myddys of ye
liver where it is hollow doth lay a little bladder yt is namyd the gall or deyned
to receive ye su{per}fluyte of Colera / it hath. ii. oryfyces / one in the
myddest of ye liver for to receive the colera. The other gothe aloge down by
the bothom of ye sto make / for to puryfye the guttys to drive out the colera.
The mylt is ordained in the left side ouerthwartly enbrasynge ye stomach / is
bound with her panycle to iii. eybbys with her back / with her hollow nes to ye
stomach The kydners be twain the one is ordernid for to purysy the blode the
watery su{per}fluyte / in them is a holownes wherein they receive such as they
draw to them. In each of them be. ii. entrees / through the one they draw ye
wate ^y humour of the vain Chyli / also from the liver. Through the other they
send vryn water to the bladder / and the kydnes be joined to the back be fat
roude about Behind the kydnes by the spodyles be the lymmes or nether rydge
bones there on restrynge as on a quylt / or matrys. Between yt kydnes passes ye
veins Chyli A dorthi to the netherm^mmes / by the which veins very ny^he
grows the semynall vessellys.

Of the flanks herpartyes Ca. viii.
Of the flanks ye shall und stand the nether part of ye belly frome the lap
to the secrete membrys / be of. ui. manners / somholde / as myrach / Siphae /
Sir bus / the bonys / some be holden / as ye semi nall vessellys / the moder or
matrix in a wo ma / the fudament gut / the senowes vay nes ye comes
downward. In every of them is a gryat bone / they be ordained together with a
great spodyle namyd ossis sacris on the back side / and on the for part
making of ye genytour bone / namyd os pectinis. Thus these bonys go abroad over
both ye sides of ye lymmes of the hyppes / where through having in the great
holys doth go both senowes / veins / strings / they be also but small by ye
side of pectinis / by the secrete members. In the myddest of them yt nether
part by the boxys or holownes / or pixides / wherein be stryngys of ye bonys.
Of the lymmes yt be holden is first ye bladder / is like a bag / where in is
gadered the su{per}flue water / or vryne / that comes of the kydneys / ye
bladder is of. ^i. strong panicles / is roundand great about the quatite of a
pynte. In it be. ii. loge ways named porri vritides / coming from the kydneys
a side half / berynge the vryne from ye kydneys. The neck or pipe of the
bladder is flesshy with closing and onclosynge lacertys or musculys / going
from the bladder beudyd through the myddys unto the yard of the man But in a
woman without beudynge / the quatyte of. ii. inches with there secrete mebre /
through that is the vryne drives.

Of the grain or semynall vessellys. Ca. ix.
THe semynalle vessellys be in them self veins / that have their beginning
by the kydneys / of the veins of Chyli and Adorati / descendynge be^ge the
blode to the coddes / both (...) man and woman / wherefore in the last^yon the
sede is namyd sperma / which is the sede of our humayne nanature. In a man
these vessellys be outwardys / for their coddys be without / and the women's
vessels be within / for their coddys or stones be within / and by this may be
marked that this sede hath the nature of the heart / the liver / and ye kydneys
and the brain / for this cause / for to make dilectacyon / the senowes com
from ye brains to the stones / also the hole body hath felowshyp therewith. The
matrix or moder is an acker of the generation of mankynd / and an organ for to
conceyne / whose manner posycyo or place is between ye bladder fudament / and is
made of. ii. strong pannycles / and is round / and hath armis with coddys or
stones like ye purse of ye coddis hath a thing like a belly i ye myddyl and a
neck holowe and small at the end like a manys yard that is crokyd / hath a
cleft namyd vulua / and hath aprepuciu or covering like a manys yard / and is
of length. viii. or. ix. inches. And though she hath. ii. holownessys yt be
openly know after the nobre of her brestys or pappis yet she hath each divided
in. iii. cellys or chabres / and one in the myddys / and thus she hath. vii.
cellys or places of coceyuyng She hath also collygacyon with the brains / heart
/ liver / and the stomach / and is bound to the back / between her and the
brestys be joined to gydder the milk and the menstruall veins. Therefore
Ypocras saith that the womans milk is the brother of mestruum. And Galienus
saith therefore that the woman can nathaue their costumable disease of menstruum
give milk at one time. Under ye moder is ye right fundament which is the
keeper of the su{per}fluyte of the first dysgestyon / and is made of panycles /
and is of the length of a shaftment / rechynge nygh to the kydneys /
stretchynge in length nyghe to the romp bonys and the undermost part of it is
namyd the ars / and the ars gut hath collygacyo with the bladder / therefore in
their sekenes they suffer with each other. The mannys y^ is a plowman of the
nature of mankynd / and is also a way of the vryne / is made of skyne /
musclus / veins / senowes / and gross stryngys / and it is plantyd upon the
bone Pectinis / and ye bondys com from the bone Sacris / or holy bone. In the
yard be. ii. pryncypall ways or pypes / the one for the sede / and the other
for the vryn. The end of the yard is namyd Ballanum the hole is namyd mitra.
The first ouergoynge skin of the yard is prepucium / and the yard is
commonly. viii. or. ix. finger breed lunge / and must be of reasonable bygnes /
according to the quantyte of the matrix or moder. Permenium or Peritonium is
the place between the ars and the yard / the which is a seem that follows
the lyne of the yard. Inguina or lyskes be ye clynsers of ye liver / ordained
in ye foldys of the thyges. Nates be the buttocks / ordained upon ye bone
semoris / and is grofe lacertous flesh.

Of the shynnes / and great fete. Ca.. x.
THe great foot or the shynne bone contynueth of ye joint Scie / or the
thyghes / to the uttermost part of the articles. This great foot is divided
in. iii. ye first is ye thygh the other is the shynne. the third is the little
foot. When the veins be descendyd with branches from their beginning to the
last spondyle or backbone / tha be they divided in. ii. parties. The one goth to
the right bray or thyghe / ye other to ye lift / and comme branch wise down
through the shynnes to the fete / and make. iiii. veins. The first is named
Sophena / of the innermest holownes of the anclewe. The secound / Sciatica on
the utter part of it. The third / Poplitica between the great too and the
other. The. iiii. is Renalis / between the little too and ye other. These veins
be let blode for divers dyseases / for this cause there be in the shynnes.
iii^. great veins that oftetymes brings in great course of blode with peril
and Jeopardye Auice. saith yt the senowes of ye fete come from ye fenowes of ye
hadys / but they take their beginning from the last spondylle of the kydneys
/ and the bone sacri. It is to be understand that by the form or dysposycyon
of musclus yt woudes by the ioyntys be peryllous / and sore to be feryd. The
gross boundys come out through ye shynys and be openly shewyde from beneth by
the knees and on the helys / and in the ioyntys of the articles / the sole of
the foot is all full of bounds.

Of the bonys in the great foot. Ca.. xi.
THe first that is namyd the thygh is a great mary bone / and round at both
the endys The uppermost roundues is named Uertebrum / and enters in ye broad
bonys of the hanches. The nether part toward ye knee has. ii. roundnessys /
which come in. ii. holownessys of the first shynne bone namyd Osfocile / and
thereon is a roud broad bone namyd the worle bone or knee shyue / and so is the
knee full made. Tha^ weth the shynne bone / and therbe. ii. (...) namyd focilia
/ ye byggest ^ former side makyd the gaderynge of ^es / and comes down from
the kn^ onto ye foot / and makes the anclewe on the inner side. The other on
the utter side like wise desce dynge shyftynge her self to the foot by the
other focili bone / and makes ye vttermeste anclewe / and these. ii. shynne
bonys make between them both one holownes / where as the first bone of the
foot is received in. And in ye foot be. iii. acyes or gaderynge of bonis In ye
first acyes be. iii. boys gadered together i one rowndnes. The first of these
iii. bonys is namyd Cahap / or Astralagus and is round onether side. In the up
permost roundness is festyned in the holownes of focilium / and there hath the
foot meuynge. In the other roundness is festyned the holownes of the bone namyd
Nauicularis. Than followed incontinent upon the foot the bone named Cahab. The
bone Nauicularis is like a shypholow on both sides. In ye first holownes is
received the roundness of the bone Cahap. In the other holownes comes the
roundness and gaderynge of the bonys of the foot. Under these. ii. bonys is made
the hole bone proporcyon of the heal / wherein is festynyd the hole foot / and
beryth outward behind for ye great bondis that be in it. Now vndstande that
after the bone Nauiculare is in continent the second hepe of the bonys of ye
foot / wherein be. iii^. short bonys / of ye which the one is namyd
Grandinosum. These bonys be round according to the bone nauiculare / and be
round toward ye third hepe of the bonys. In the third hepe be v. bonys loge
/ and receyuynge the articles of the toes / which be also. v. in nombre / each
hath. iii. bonys save ye great toe has but. ii. bonys. Thus there be in the
little ^te. xxvi. bonys. And in the hole great foot be. xxxviii. bonys. Thus may
a surgyon mark by this / howe he should break dysmembre / and join again
together / among all other the little foot is most dangerous to dysmembre /
and set again together / and the lyghtest is the knee / and the myddelmost is in
the thyghe. (...).

Here endyh the Anothomia of the body of a man / for to know ye cuttynge /
dysmembrynge and ioynynge again Here after follows the science and conyn^ of
Surgery




Of the helynge of small vuoudis, Ca, xii.
AFter the declaracio that is made of the Anathomia / ye shall understand that
I will begyne by ordre the handworke of surgery / first I will begyne with the
woudes / that be hewydor betyn only through the skyne unto the flesh / how ye
shall demeue your self to cure and heal them by the grace of god. Compelle and
join the lyppes of the woudes together (...) your hand / and lay tow thereto
with the white of an egg / tempered with a little common salt and bind it
according to the need. The woudyd joint must rest and be holdyn styll / for
through rest it must be cured or else other accydentis will put back your cure
through effusyos or corrup cyos of blode / non other curing is of need so that
the woude be without payne and ye depth well dysposyd / but if there be great
pair in it / for that should be a tokyn that the fas in the depth were hurt /
or the pannycle that is between the flesh and the bone which covers the
bone. Mark the words of Guidonis that saith / ye shall never begyne to heal a
would till all other ipedimetis be first voydyd from it / which to fallyngis or
accidentis happen most in great woundis.

Of the stichyng^ or festenynge of great woudis in the flesh. ca. xiii.
When there come to ye any great woude / that is not only through the skyne /
but also through ye flesh unto ye bone / without and to fallyngis or
accidetis. Than shyft the lyppes of it together proply and clean / and tha
festyne them according to their need. which festenynge may happen in diverse
manners whereof I will writ the most common. If the wound be than so great that
that byndynge only ware not enough for it. Or if ye wound were over twhart a
hole (...) / and that the lyppys of the wound drew ^de a sonder / might not be
bound together. Than shyfte ye lyppys or vpperparte of the woudis together / and
beware there come no manner of onclennes of dust / here / oil / nor non other
thing that the gadered helynge thereby might be let. Than take a iii. square
nedyll as the skyners occopy / and se that the nedyll be holowe graven out
about theiye / so that ye thread that shall go therein may lay flat in ye
holownes. The thread shall also be twyned together without any knottys waxed
wherewith ye shall festyne / and the feste / nynge is in. v. manners. First the
common festenynge as to the foresaid belongs / is that ye shall set the first
stiche in ye myddis of the woundys lyppys / the other a finger broad between
every. ii. stiches / and so to the end till there be stiches enough / but
begyne never at the end / thentent that the woude may be ye purer festenyd
^out any fro^cys. Therefore ye stiches shall be always add whather behooves more
tha twain Also ye shall vnderstade when ye woude is deep ouertwhart / than must
ye styches be ye deper festenyd for. ij. manner of causes / the first is because
that it should breast out ye less. the second it should matter the less / and
because yt should be the less holownes vnderneth. Ye shall not need to feste
it deep if ye woude be of length. And when ye have festenyd ye woude / se that
ye over cast your thread twyse or ye knet the knot / for else it would breast
out again or ye cowed knet it / as I have scene oftyn of vnlernyd surgeons /
but ever keep your finger upon it till it be fast knet that ye be not deceived
with one knot / but when it is overcast as before is said / ye need not to fere
the yeopardy. And when that ye have done as I have let nydin the stychynge as
before is said / tha do after my co^soll and folewe these noble lernyd men and
surgeons / as Lafrancus / Guido / Guilhelm? / Placeti^ de saliceto / do their
comaudemet and fail not to bear upon you this powder. A Powder. made of white
franckencence. ij. parties / dragons blode. i. part / and one third ^te of lyme
made of egg shellrs / make all these in one powder and temperit with ye white
of an egg / lay that on ye wound with tawe / though it have not be used till
this time but with the white of anegge salt. But this fornamyd powder is much
better and profitable. and this is the first manner for to stiche ye woudis. The
second manner is to sow over hand as ye skyners do / that fortunes in ye
bowels or sypha^ that is the call that keep the bowels each by other. The
third manner is for to put the nedyll through both the lyppys of the woude /
and let the nedyll bide therein stic king / and than take the thread and wynd
it about both the endis of the ne^yll. vi. or vii. times / and let it bide so
styll as lunge as it nedis / as it fortunes in wide or large woundis. The
fourth manner is that sometime a stychynge or festynynge happens for to stauche
blode / and that is when ye se a vain blede sore / as the vain of the neck /
or ye vouded betynge vain / thrust that vain through with the nedyll / and
after the nedyll / knet the vain fast with ye thread that is in the nedyll /
than draw the nedyll through / and let an end of the thread bide hagynge at
it a certain days till that upper part of the vain doth putrifye / and that
ye thread go out by him self. The. v. manner hapeneth in the face / or in such
place as would not be scene / and also in tether people that were not able to
suffer the fornamyd stychynges / and eke in great woudis that have ye lyppis
wide a souder thus if shall be ordered. Take little lynnen cloutys three square
and spread them (...) this salve / made of dragatu / dragons blode / Olibanu /
Masticis / Sarcocolle / of each one dragma. Myldust out of the mile three
dragmas. The white of an egg so much till it be ynowgh. Than lay upon every
side of the woude the pecys eueriche of them an inch from other. And when ye
cloutis be well dry / tha sow them or styche them together. Thus endyth th is
chaptuor of the stichynge or festynge of ye small or simple woudis / that be
chased in the skyne / or in the flesihe.



Of the woundys in senowes. ca. xiiii.
First it is to be regardyd whether the woude be in ye length of the senowe or
in the breed. Or that it is only a prycke with a nedyll / an alle / thorne / bod^
kynor any such like. Or that the senowe is over twharthewed clean of / or cut.
Or that it be cut through ye length. Nota when the senowe is hurt with a foyne
/ than is the woude close. than it is need to make the woude wyder and put
therein oil of rosys made with on^ype oil oylue / wermer tha he may well
suffer it. so lunge till the woude be full. furthermore yt shall be laid to the
woude fyn turpetyne that is pure / white / and well washed between. ij.
clothes. and ye woude and lyme about it

A Salve.
shall be enoynted with that warm oil of rosys temperyd with bolo armeno that
it may be some what thycke. thereupon shall be laid a soste lynen clothe yt hath
beu wet before in good warm white wine / tha bind it up softly. And if the
payne do not cease with this at the syrst / than do it oftyn yt it cease for
there is no better way / though ye payne vanysh not incotinent. This doth
Lanfrancke testefy / and many other noble surgeons. But if the payne contyne we
to lunge / than it is good be my coucell for to take oleum rosa^ / boli armeni
and opium thebaicum a little / and made warm / and occopyed in the fornamyd
manner. And the pacyent shall rest and meue but little / and keep him self from
anger. And whane the payne doth cease / and the woude draw to ye draught / Than
heal it with the grene woude salve and wound drink / the which I will show
you herafter in ye antithodari^ Nota / if ye senowe or ye vain be hewyd / or
cut a soder / tha festyn ye vain or senowe in such manner as the lyppes of ye
woudes be festenyd if that ye can get the vain with woude / upon the vain
woude ye shall lay oil of roses made with grene oil olyue where as ye little
groude wormys be sodt in / and howe ye shall sethe them ye shall know in the
Antithodario / and that shall ye use. ij. or. iij. days / and on the. iiij.
day take the foresaid powder that is showed in the. xiij. chapter of the
festenynge of ye woudis made in this manner. Of white frankecence c. but it were
very vtyle and profytable to put among it the powder of dried worms before
namyd / dried to the uttermost without brenynge. But the dryenge that naturally
behouyth to the woudis of senowes and veins as Lanfrancus / Guido / and
Rogerius testefye / is vnguentum de vermibus / made in this manner.

A Salfe
Take little Centaurea Lingua canina herba / consolidamator / consolidamedia /
an hafull of each / a pownde of grene oil olyue ground worms half a li.
whytt wine half. li. stamp all these together and let it stand stepynge in
himself. vii. days / and than ye shall stamp with it. ij. li. of shepis
talowe / black pytche rosyn / a quarter of each. Armoniaci / Galbani /
appoponati / meltyd in vinegre. v. dragmas of each / sethe all these together
till the wine vinegre be consumed / than strain it / and when it is almost
cold / than put to them half a quarter of turpentyn / frankencence / mastic /
sarcocolle. iij. dragmas of each. ij. drag mas of saffran / and take a spatula
styrie all these together / and thus make this salve for it is very precyo^ i
necessite. Roger? doth put to this millefolin / but Lafcancus comaudeth yt ye
shall keep ye woude moist first. ij. or. iii. days with oil of rose groude
worms when the wound is festenyd. This ointment following thou ought for to
have always by ye for to anoint about the woundis / for all conynge surgeons use
it for to defend all fresshe woundis.

A deffencyfe salfe.
And the deffencyf is made in this manner. Take. iiii. ouces of oliu Rosaru. ii.
ouces of boli armeni / terra sigillata / asceti / of each of them an ouce /
canfer one dragma / night schae / hows leke / of each an handful. Of all
these ye shall make a fine oynt met in a mortyr / for through these for said
festenynge of the senowes / and through ye oil / powder ointment / the lyme is
preseruyd helyd / and rectifyeth. Also ye shall not be to sore abasihyd of the
pain that comes of the pryckynge of the nedyll / for ye payne is swetnyd
again with the oil of Rosys when it hath been anointed there with iii. or. iiii.
times. But if the payne do not seas / that is a tokyn of the cramp or a cut
tynge of the senowe* Now may ye re^ue me of that I said before / that the oil
was a deffendour of the helyng of the woudis / because I docomaunde here to put
warm Rose oil in the wound / also abuut it. But to this I answer / Though
Galien{is} saith that the wounds ought to be taken heed of yt there come no
here / nor oil / nor other fylthenes / Therefore I say that ye oil of rosys
must be made of grene or on type oil olyue yt seems more a ioyst or lycour
than oil / and of the ground worm the oil receives a conglu^nacyon. Ye
shall never begin to heal up the woudetyll ye payne be passyd and gone / sor
if ye heal it up or the payne be passyd and gone / it is to be feared that an
i^ os^ume and swellynge with great hete / shall stryke to ye woude / and of
that to falling it fortunes so time the loss of a limb or death. The
surgeon may do no better for ye ease of the dyseasyd pson / but to keep the
wooded lyme from swellynge with great hete as it is before said Is that the
wound done not heal with ye for said oil and powder / that ye woude
dydonclose and began to matter or come to draught / than shall ye heal the
woude with the grene woudis salve which I will set in the antithotarius / and
that salve shall be stryked upon a lynen clothe and laid to ye woude at morn
and at night / and in the nedermost end of the woude / ye shall put a little
tent / yt the senowes be not meuyd or touched that there come no payne of it.
If that there were of yt matter to great a supsluyte than make this salve
following / the which doth not only purifye the woudis of the senowes / but
also all manner of woudes / though it were in a deep holowe woude / which salve
shall be made in this manner. Take strained rosehony. vi. oucis fine boultyd barley
flower. ii. ouncis / temp these together and sethe them / but loke that brene
not. And when ye have set it from ye fire / stere it well with a spatulum and
put thereto. ii. ouncis of white turpentyne* or if ye find no white / than
wasshe it in cold water till it be whyt / but for that common water I have take
one of these water that I could get best / as Sanicle water / small planteyn
water / consolida minor water / sidou wat rose wat. when ye would lenyth of
matterynge will dry / A salve. Tha take of ye forenamyd salve. iiii. oucis
whyt frankencens dragons blode / mastic / sarcocolle / a dragma of each /
temper them all together / and lay it to the wound as be fore is said. till it
be hole / and always lay above the woude / tow / stepyd in strong whyt wine /
well warm / that defedyth the wonde from all accedentis / payne swell ling and
hete / specyally when in the wine is sodyn Consolida mayor mouseer with ye gelow
flowers / and sent Johns wort with the brodleuys. If the common veins ve hurt
that be namyd vene or arteria whihe be the betynge veins / They may so sore
hurt that they shall never be helyd trwly / as some doctors say / But that
fortunes whane they be woudyd ouertwhart / But they be hurt in length / they
may be helyd truly / as it is opynly enough known by the veins yt belet
blode / which be helyd in few days without dryenge powders. But to heal the
woudyd veins is done with the for namyde powder that is made of the dried ground
wormys named Lombrici / and that laid in the woundr / and the forsayde rose
oil soden with the groude worcester mys laid warm upon it with cotton. Hereof I
have had much profit / also scene it of many good masters / though yt some
say that ye wormys should be brent to powder / but it is nothing so / but
they shall be dried in an ouyn where as ye breed is drawn out of till ye may
bray them to powder / For when they be brent to powder they less their strenght
of their coglutina cyon or gaderynge together of flesh / But they gader ye
skyne to soon toge^ / ye which to ye grieved senowes is no need. This fortunes
also in ye salve aforsayd of the said worms / as Lacfracus Guido testefied.

Tostaunce blode in the woundyd veins. Ca. xv
IF it fortunes yt vene capillares / which be the smallest veins / or vene
maiorum / which be the great blode veins / or are terie / that be the betyng
veins were hurt / and died blede sore / thane is it needful that ye behold
the manner of the woundyd man / the complexcyon / the age / the strength of
youth / specyally ye must mark if he have much blode in his body / than let
enough go out of it / if ye be called thereto betyme. But if ye come not intyme
by him / so that he through fawte of blode should become faint feeble / tha
mark if ye blode come from venis capillariv{is} / for they be veins as small
as heer / if it so do / tha after ye stitchynge of ye woude / it is s^ffycy ent
to lay to it / the white of an egg with tow with the powder before namyd /
for that powder stauncheth blode and cogluti nesh the lyppys of ye woude
together. When the blode comes from the great vain named vena matoru / thane it
comes slowly forth / it is gross / and enclyneth him to a purpre colour /
blackysshe / when it is not stauched / it is dedly / for the blode is ye tresour
of the life. And Auicena writes that if ye woudyd {per}soon have any of these
chau ches / that is to say Spasmus which is ye cramp / or Cincopis that is
the swowyng it is a suspect tokyn or sign / Also when ye blode comes from
the artery / which is the betyng vain / ye shall know it by this tokyn / for
the blode commyth spryngynge out / like as the vain closyth and open^* If it
be not staunchyd lyghtely / the won did parson bledyth him self to death.
Therefore it is not enough always to use the fornamyd staunchynge of blode. But
this vein behooves a mighty strong stauchyng of blode / yt may be done in. ii.
manners. Therefore we can not vndstade yt ye blode of ye woude ca be stauchyd only
with the drynes yt be laid to ye woude as it is before said. But ye shall have
therefore a rule / where with the cowrs of ye blode may be helped stoppyd / yt in
many sondry ways / sometime it fortunes that it will be helped with byndynge
of the contrary side over against yt woundyd place sometime with rubbing /
sometime with lettynge blodr in another place / sometime with boxinge / sometime
with ymagynacyo / that she woudyd parson doth imagine or think that he bledid
nomore. The second rule or manner is how ye shall use the utter more dryenge /
namyd the localia / howe it should be laid upon the woude and vain / and this
is of divers manners occupied ruled / sometime with noise that causes one to
start for fere that the blode roneth or congelyth / or the dryenge be laid to
it / sotyme it dries with fasting of the vain with the nedyllor the tread /
sometime with brenynge with other ways as ye shall here. when ye have dressyd a
woude with the drink substances before namyd / that it will not stauche / than it
is necessary for to remedy the cowrs of ye bledynge / in this manner / ye shall
bind and rub the cotrarye part as if the right hand did blede / than ye
should rub the lift arm well up and down / and after that rubbing bind it
with a woollen selue ege of clothe to tentent that the blode may ron to succour
the place that is so fore boude because that the other place so bledyng may
stauche / but not sully / for if it were hole stoppyd / the lyme or place might
ware styffe and less his feeling and be as deed. And thus may ye do from ye lift
hand to the right / and frome ye right side of the heed to the lift foot / and
in ye same manner may be done with boxyng fleemynge / also with closing of the
woudyd parson or with setting at wyndow his heed outwardis that he se no manner
of red / and say always to him that he bledyth nomore / than ye died fleem him
or let him blode for his health. And thus is ye natural strength enforcid /
blode stauched through the contrary ymagynacyon / and this is ye first manner
for to stauche ye flode of bledig The other manner or rule is how ye ought to
order your pacyent in the localia / that is in the laynge on of the dryinge
substance or syccatyf without with the hand. And this is done in many manners.
Galien{is} in qui to terapeti / Lanfrancus of myllayne / Gui do / conclude all
together that in the cour^ of the blode which can not be stauched with the for
said mysterijs / than lay your finger softh upon the mouth of the woude of the
vain / holding it styll till ye blode do ron or gely / or ye lay any drynes
or syccatyf to it. The other manner or rule is yt ye shall have always by your
powder that of their own nature doth stauche or restrain the blode / that the
powder have in him self such strength that when it towcheth the vain / that
it therewith may close / which strength is namyd stiptica / and that causes
also the flesh to grow. Another manner following / is that if ye cane get ye
vain by the end and festene it / as it is showed before in the. xiii.
chaptre. Another manner to brene the end of the vain that it may have an estra
which is a skurffe or shrynk^ ge together / that is in. ii. manner of ways. The
syrst is done with sharp dryeges or cy catyffes / as with vitriole / bret or onbret
/ or else with vnslycked lyme. The second with a breninge yro or gold which
belogeth to ye vain / as saith Aui. The hot cauteriu shall be done in this
manner with a hot brenyn ge yro yt it be deep to thetent it may make a gros estra
or skurffe / whose offallyng be natheuy. The cauterys or yros yt ye brene with be
figured here vnderneth / and ye need nomore instrumetis than here be figured /
for over many doth trouble.



Theodoric{is} praises Arcenicu sublimaticum with such brenynge / for that
stops all great flode of ye blode / also it makes aloge during estram or
scurffe. Another is that ye must lay that lyme right that it hang not as ne'er
as it is possible. Also if it hath bled much before / take it not of in iii.
or four days till ye vain be somewhat helyd. And take your bynding is of
wisely and not rechelessy lest ye hurt the vain cause it to brene upon a
fresshe. If that ye syccatyffes or byndynges be taken to it / tha ye shall lay
wet things to it an howr of twain because ye should not hurt your pacyent /
nor trowble your self / ye must do it thus / take the white of an egg / and
vile of Roses well betyn together / and lay yt to it / or else take a fair
lynen clowte deep it in wine and lay that to it. Another manner of dryeng as
this / ye shall lay your finger upon the mouth of the vain till the blode
besomwhat run that it be thycke / and than must ye have a powder

A siccatyf powder
Made of pure whyt frackencens. ii. partis Aloepaticum. i. part / temper this
powder with the white of an egg as thycke as honey / and deep therein white
haers hee^ yt is cut small and lay that to the woude or vain / for that doth
not only stauche the blode / but yt helyth also the arteries / as Lanfrancus of
melan hath often times provide / as he writes in the chapter of ye staunchynge
of wounds / that a child of iii. year old having a knyf in his hand / and
sell upon it and so hurt him self in ye throat / unawares he com by the
child which all ready had lost his sight / and the blode died ron white out
of veins / and his puwlce died beat but fayntly / and he laid incontynente
his finger upon the mowthe of the wound that there might nomore yssowe out the
wound / and with in alystonde the nature was reconfortith / and ye poulce
began to beat again / the iyen began to opyn / than died he lay the fornamyd
powder upon the wound / and upon that he died lay tow depyd in ye white of an
egg / and he commaundyd to give ye child a morssell of bred stepyd in water /
the next day the child was well strengthyd / yet he unbound not the bound
till the fourth day after / and on the. iiii. day the drynes or cyccatyf was
so harde back there to / that he cowed not well get it of. Tha he did lay to
it the white of an egg oil of rosis betyn together as before is said and did
let it lay upon it till the next day and than was the woude clean hole /
whereof all the people therabout had great marvel. If the blode will not
stanch with such cyccatyffes through any accydentys or tofallynges / tha
must ye work with such sharpe ferynges or brennyngys as is before specyfyed.
Also another stauchyng takyn by the instruccyo of Auicenna / A cyccatyf powder
Take onquenchyd lyme / dragos blode aloes succotrini / of each a like much /
and thereof a powder made / and used as ye other before. If ye will have another
that dries and resteyneth more.

A powder.
Take a great gall apple / drages blode voly armeni / frakecece / aloepatic^ /
mastie of all these a like much / and thereof a powder made / and to it / put
the guarter of as much whyt harys heer that is cut small and that occupied
in the for said manner. Another powder that Rogerius / Jamerius used / ye
which doth not only stau the blode but also it doth dry heal.

A Powder.
Take grek is pytche. vi. ouces / boli armeni. iii. ouces mastic / dragos blod
/ olibanian ouce of each / ye rote of cosolida mayor / roses of each an half
ounce / of all these make a fine powder / and use it as before is she wy^ After
this I will show you of many and diverse powders at more layser in ye
Antithodarius. Of all the staunchyngys of blode thateuer I se / I never saw
none better than one stone that is brought out of spain or galisce not far
fro ye way to saint Jamys which I used / as soon as I towched the mowthe of
the wound or vain / it staunchyd and closyd / butt I toke also of ye same
stone puluerysed strewed that powder round about it in the mean season that ye
stone was in it / when I would occopy it again / thadyd I pullys she the stone
(...) of ye old blode (...) it was fres^he again. also. ij. {per}tys of this
pow^ myxed among one part of the other and so used hath done me great
pleasure at my most ^e is very profytable / this stone is somewhat palewhyt /
and hath sometime in it small rede veins / and is namyd of ye pelgrymes the
blode stone / but it is not the stone Jaspis nor Ematites / and when the blode
is so staunchyde / the wound helyth as before is specyfyed.

Of the wounds where thornys spletys / or such like be in. Ca xvi.
IF now there were no vain hurt nor no flode or course of blode / that there
were between the {per}tys of ye woude a piece of a bone / a piece of ye arowe /
thorne / a splynter / that the wound were to narow. Tha it is need for you to
cut or make the mowthe of it more wyder / that in two manners. The first with a
tent made with ye rote of gencyane / or pyth of el^ or of a we^e piece of a
spoge boude hard (...) a thread and dried upon an iron / and tha the thread
taken of again / and here of make tentys / one smaller than another / occopy
th^m till ye have made the wound as big as need requires / or as ye desire.



The second manner is / that ye shall cut the wound wyder with a pair of
cysars or with sheres there to belonging / as here is figured / but that is
dredfull to the wou did {per}son^ counsel fo^ But if those ca nateas / yt ye
diseasyd {per}soon ca not for great feer abide ye cutting / Tha must ye make
this sleep drink and give it him to drink / whereof he shall (...) in sleep and
feel another cuttynge nor payne / thus must y^ make it.

A sleep drink.
Take ye rote of Solatru mortale / semen i^s^ami of each an ouce / white popy
sede / blak popy sede / opiu the baicu adragma / croci orietalis / corticis
madragora / lignu aloes / Cinamomi / Castoriu / a dragma of each. And of all
these make a course powder / and of this powder take. ij. dragmas and i^ ^e it
with maluesye / give it him at a draght. And when he is in sleep than cut up the
woude as much as nedyth till it be wide (...). Tha draw out such thing as
is in it with thy fyngers or with nipers. In the same manner gone stones / with
nypers or pynsons and other instrumentis as here after is more plainly
expressyd / And when thou will have him wakend again tha put a piece of a sponge
in his nose / that hath ben wet in vine gre or in ye Joyst of Few or fenell /
and there with all he wakens again. Some give him Opiu alone without any other
thing therein tempered / but beware thereof / for some become frantycke or made
thereof / thus it is very daugerous. If that the woudis were made wide with the
tentis or with the cuttynge that they were not wide enough / and that ye durst
make it no wyder with cuttig through fear of death / or leasing of a ^oynte /
than put into the woude this instrument balista yt is here figured / wherwt ye
shall enlarge it / and than ye may put your Instrument into the woude and take
out that is in it.

Of (...) ^is shot with poisoned ^ he dis and other thyngis ca. xvii.


When any pacyent comes to you / this is my coucell that ye demand of him /
howe and in what manner this chance died fortune him / in what manner and form
that this is shot or other wise come to him / as of ye things yt therein be
remained / like glass / iron / thor^e / arow heed / or other divers things /
some be right / sum crooked / some round / some hoked / sum square / some
triangled / some holowed where timber has ben in / sum venymed / and some
not venymed. Some stycke fast in the flesh / some in the bone / some so deep in
the body that it go the almost through both the sides. And when ye be well
assured of these / than it is need yt ye have some instrument in your besynes be
longing to this work. Of the which ye first be tongues or nypers / half moan
wise and inwardly tothed.



The other be ryhgt terebellys sharp before / like as ye se figured and
counterfayted here benythe / when the heed of the arow is broken of / than ye
may pierce with your instrument in the timber softly and so draw it out.



The other be nypers or pynsons / namyd Albucasys / and is formed like the bill
or nebbe of a stork within dentyd teeth which is figured as it is shewyde by
this instrument that stondyth here benethe between ye other. ii.

The other be tongues or nypers that be broad / indentyd and holowe as che nebbe
/ for to take out a gone stone / like as here stondyth benethe on the other
side.

The other be terebellys yt be viced going in a pipe / like as it stodith
figured here be nethe on ye one side / and it is for to take an arow heed out
when the wode is out of it.



THe manner in such cause to work is this. Thou shalt mark ye tokens of life
or death or ye shall begine to work yfye se any toke of death / tha take
nothige out of the body at that time for fere of death before he hath taken his
sacrament. The first toke / as when the shot is in the heed brain / so suffer
the pacyent great payne whereby the s^ome avoid out of the mouth and at the
woude. That other token / as the shot is in the heart / so commyth there out
black blode. The third token / as the shot is in the loungis / than there
comes scomynge blode out. The. iiii. token / as the patient is towchyd in
the maw / than gothe his meet vndisgest out. The. v. token / as the paciet is
towchyd in his guttis so he auoydyd his tordre out. The. vi. token. as the
patient is towchyd in his bladder / so he avoid out his water / and that is a
sign of death / And in all other places there the patient is hurt / there as
the sign of death is not pull out of the wound that shot / as I shall learn
you. and than heel it as another wound. And that shot shall be taken out in
sondry manners. And there is iii. principal manners of takenout. The first that
must be taken out with tongys and instrumetis. The. ii. that with might is
smitten through coming out on ye other side. The. iii. is / as the shot will
not come out / or may not be draw out without more harm / and you may not
make the woude greater with cuttynge or with tentys. So let the wound certain
days putrifye / so comes the shot better out / Nevertheless it must be
handled softly / and there upon ley the plaster drawing to the sore / as I
shall learn you If it be so that an arow is poisoned / if any body is shoten
with a gone / so do as I shall learn you. ye which drawn with plasters it will
not be well done with out the woude be wyder made with cuttynge or with tentys.
Also saith Henricus that it may be hastly drawn out. And so saith Auicenna /
Albucasis / and Brunus. And there after may ye heel the wound as ye will
heel an other woude / No more there to do than the superfluence blode which is
become to matter in the wound / that it be clensyd. If ye be in fear of
coming more payne / so may ye put in the wound hot oil often times. And as
ye will begyne to work / ye have knowledge whether it be an arowe / or a gone
pylleth / or another thing. And if the shot is in ye heed with any other dyseas
or to falling / so draw the arowe out craftily with a pyle tongge like as here
to fore the pyctor or figure shows. Is any body shot in the arm or leg /
and the tymbre be from the iron / so cut that other side against the wound /
draw out that iron. If he be shot in his body and the tymbre be out of his
body fro the iron / than must you ^erche the iron with a tongue or a small
instrument of iron where that it is / Than draw it proprely out / If ye woude
be to narrow than may ye do as is aforesaid with tentys or cutting / If he may
suffer it waking or slepynge / so draw it out with your instrument / If it may
not so be / ley there upon a plaster / give the pacyent a drink as I shall
learn you in this chaptre / also in Anthidotario The patient shall lye upon ye
woude as he may best suffer / because that ye said drink and plaster may the
better draw out the iron / And as ye may {per}ceyue ye yro / draw it out.
Never shall you pull out ye shaft fro the iron as one is shot with an arrow. If
the shaft be shot deep in the body / in the plu^ king out of the arrow ye
leese the iron of the arrow so that ye can not find it. So it was be happened
king Mathyse of hugri was shotten with an arrow in ana^me the timber cam out /
and ye y^on cowed not be found / The said king {pro}^ysyd who that cowed get
out that iron without harm doing he would give them great good. Tha cam to him
hans dockenborth and dressed ye woude there he was shotten in / and band him so
that there cam no matter out fro the woude in many days / and leyd upward above
ye woude an defensyfe a cold plaster

An defensyfe.
Made of bolo armeno / vynegre / camfere / a little roose oil / and ye white
of an egg myxed made as thycke as honey / because ye arm shulde not festre in
fire / by reason of the byndynge caused to gadder the matter about the iron in
the woude / so the skyne swellyd / where by the iron cam / there cut he the skyne
and toke out the yro without any tongue. Than the king made him knight an earl.
Wherefore ye masters remember upon it as ye can not find ye iron / or yt it be
in a such place that ye may not cut. yfit be in arm or leg / Is the timber
be goo out and ye iron is bide within / put therein that instrument called a
terebell in apype / and shrouyd upward and pull that iron out. If yt may not
be done so / make the woude wide with tenttys / or with cuttynge / and so may
ye pull it out. But first put in the wound that instrument called Balista /
and there after the terebelle / because it shall to softer goo in. And if that
iron will not come out lyghtely when ye begyne to pull tha prove it with the
pyll tongue / and as ye have the iron with the tongue / and it will not come
following / like as it happenyth in the borgonysshe fylde before Bloumoude that
a ma was shotten with an arowe / the iron bide in the body and the tymbre was
out / To the which was many surgeo called for help to have the yro out / it
would not follow / than cam there to a surgeon of Straesborowe called Hans
mayere / and he toke the pyltonge in his hand / and he {per} ceyuyd that the
iron was hoked cross wis and he turned the iron with the tongue about so that
the crossyd iron cam to ye same place as it went in / incotynent cam the yro
out / where by he was sore praysyd / yet cowed no {per}son tell how he had it
out.

If it be also that it is not possible so to do with that pulling out. And if it
be al most through going unto the further side / like yt happen the arowe to
stytche in the leg and the tymbre is still in it / than sin yte the arow
through it / and pull it out on ye other side. And if the tymbre be out than
stryke ye yro with another arowe through. so must ye do like wise if such a case
of an arowe happen in ye body / and yt is more peryllous And if an iron ware
sounke deep in the body of a man / that it were not possible to take it out
with pyle togis nor with plasters nor with tentis / nor with cuttyngis where as
it went in / nor unto the other side with outfere / so lunge let that iron
styke unto ye time that the natour will drive him out to appear. Albucasis
writes of many personis that arow heedis gon pylleth that remain in the body
/ and has worn it many a day without harm. There hath been scene in
wertenborw a Taylor that had an nedyll in his back berynge more than. xx.
winter or it was cut there of /

Of the drynes ye which pull out / thorns / splyntis / glass / bonis / and
pyces of bonys / hath Guido made one drynes / taken out of Auicenna / is made
in this manner / And all this {per}^ellis that is in ye book that ye understand
not / ye shall find it in the pottycarris to sell.

A cicatyffe powder.
Take whet me le and honey the fulness of a be heue of each a pode weght / of
bird lyme take. viii. oucis / and oil olyue viii. oucis / armoniacum. iiii.
oucis / and make thereof a salve / and use it like aforsayd is.

Salve
Make this following salve yt to him pullyth al manner of yro that bids in
manes body. Take apostomaticu Nicolay. iiii. oucys. Magnete stone which comes
fro ^iente. ii. oncys. and yelow Iye front / Polipodium / dyptami albi / of
each a half ouce. hare grese. ii. ouc. oil of hempsede an once / turpantyn a
half ouce / of al this make a plaster and lay it on the wound. Ite Rogerius
said that he hath provide / ye rote of a reed stampyd with honey and laid it to
the wound / that pull out all that is bonys / stones / glass / without any
payne. Is the wound to narrow so make it wyd with cuttynge or withe tentys as
I have before said. If that may not be done / so let the wound in him self
type with ye maturatyse / than it comes out of ye woude with ye matter / and
than cleanses the wound / if it be need do as is before said. Item here I will
learn you a marvelous mixture of many virtues / for it will suck draw out all
rotten bonys / thornys / and other like things.

A salve
Take the kyrnels of a date tree Surach rubei / sal armoniacum / lunge hole
root or astrologia longa / radicis cucumeris / asinini / terpentyn of each. v.
dragnes. and black pepper and white pepper armoniaci amoni / phylobalsa^ / tu^is
masculi / colofonie / / more tresap / of each two dragnes and a half / wax.
iiii. dragnes and ye dreggis of the oil of white lyllyes as much as ye need,
and of all these make a salve / and ley it upon the wound / and it is very
good to set on the wound a bore without pryckynge.

Of woudis that be shot with poyseneth arrow hedis and many other things. Ca.
xvii.
A Man shotien with a poisoned arrow or any other weep. and you have take out
