woude with a grene wooded plaster / and over the plaster lay a clothe dept in
warm rose oil / or in warm wine / for the warm wine doth strong / the
flesh growing as over the powder be laid the plaster / his meet and drink
shall be as is a foresaid / ye joints of ye toes shall be ryghted again like as
the Joyntes of the fyngers. As Haly wrythed.

Of the bowing of the bonys without brekynge. Ca. lxxvi.
THe bowynge of ye bonys happens sometime with falling sometime with strokes.
or with cuttynge without brekynge as the bowynge on the cheke than cirest it
outward with your hand fyngers / as I have lernyd in the chaptre of the
brekynge of the rybbes. in ye. lxix. chap. and the other hand shall be salved
with turpentyn / or pytche / and lay it without on ye cheke bone. and with the
other hand^ ^rest it softly from within outward / and take away with hast
your salved hand fro his cheke. In like wise do in the bowynge of ye rybbes.
but in the bones of the shyne or arm must ye have a good byndynge / strong
splentes / that with the thressyng of the byndyng may be ryghteth the bone again.
and the bone in the arm or leg shall be stretchyth out by little and little.
but that mebre shall first be batheth in water therein is sodden Camomyll /
Pappyll / hye malowe Fenygreke / Lynseed. And than salve it with oil of Lylyes /
or Capons grese / or Duckys grese. And it is often proved / and it helps
much / as upon the bowynge be laid a piece of an Olyphantes teeth / for ye
yuore bone pullyth to him the bowyd bone / and therewith the bone gets his
right form.

Of the dyslocacyon or dysmenbrynge of every joint in general. Ca. lxxvij


AUicenna saith / the dyssocacie or dysmembryng is an outgoyng of ye bone out
his right place there it was set in before. And the setting of the bone is in.
iiij. manners. that also Lanfranc. Wilhelm{is} / and other masters saith. The
one is after the manner of a saw with the tethes set in to gyder and so closing /
as be the. vi. bones of the braynpan. The other. as ye one bone in the other
standed and is there in set / as the tethes in the cheek. The. iij. is one
hanging or lenynge bone on another bone as the. vii. bones of the breast. The.
iiij. manner. the one bone is joined with another / bound to gyder with the
synewes / where through the meuynge of the body comes. This gaderyng of ye
bones is called a joint or mebre. In this last manner is done ye very
dyslocacye / but in the other it is not be done / but there happenyth a
dysmembrynge This dysmebringe is in iiij. manners. forward / behyndeward /
inward / outward Also is some simple / some with a fracture / payne and
impostumacyon / and some with hardness. After this dyuersyte be divers cures. And
the dysmembryng happens sometime without / as with falling / smytyng or with
unreasonable pulling. Some dysmebrynge is inward^ / as the ^ymy humours in the
joint be holden. The token of the dismembrynge of the joints is known by ye
hyghnes / or holnes on the other part. The dysmembrynge with a wound / payne
/ or impostumacyon is heavy and peryllous / so ye mebre bids sometime crooked
without tournynge again in his right form (as Galien{is} wrythet in quarto
Therapentice) The old and harde dismembering is for (...) heavy and shantely to
help / and ye must t^ membre set in again with good manner / (...) with the
lest payne as hastily as it may be done Some dysmembringe is lyghtely to set in
again / as the joint of the hands. Some dysmembrynge is heavy to set in again /
as the elbow / the foot / and the fyngers.

Some is between both / as the shoulder and hyppes. The incomynge of the membre
is known by hearing of the crakynge in ye incomynge of the bones and as ye se
that it is come in his right place in the other bone The come cure of all
dysmembrynge in the joints is in. iiij. manners. beside the lerninge that I
have given you in the chaptre of the come brekynge in the bonys. The first
manner / is the setting in again ye joint. The ^de is fast making of the
membre that there is setin again. The. iii. is defending of the payne and
impostumacyon. The. iiij. is mendynge of the ill accydetes. The first is done
in. iij. manners. The first. that ye have all thing ready by you yt is needful
to you as I have learned you in ye lix. chaptre. of all fractures in the bouys
in come or ye begin ye membre to setin again The other / that ye ye membre not
bathe nor wasshe in warm water (as Auicen. saith) that no impostumacyo come
thereto / nor let tynge to setin the membre again. Lancfracus and Wylhelmus de
saliceto saith / that some the dysmembryng as it is fresshe / than they lay that
membre in warm water a loge time / and than they setin ye mebre again and this
shall ye not do. but is the dysmembrynge some days past / than may ye bathe the
joint in warm water therein is sodden Papple / Camomylle / Hye malowe /
fenygreke / and than shall it be setin again.

The. ii. manner is done in. ii. manners. The first. as the setting in of the
joint is small and light / than is Enough to lay thereon a clothe depte in oil
of roses / and there with salved the joint / and over the clothe tow dept in
white of eggs. than bind it with a band that thereto belongs. The other. is
ye membre great and strong / and the set tynge in is heavy / and ye fere the
going out of the joint again / than ye must you provide better / therefore
anoynte the joint / and lay thereupon this plaster following.

A plaster.
Take Mylstur meell. vi. parts. Dragos blood / Frankesence / Masticke /
Satcocol le / of each one part / all this made in po^d and meddled with the
white of eggs / and stryke it upon a clothe / lay it on ye joint and
plumacioles oft^w or clothes. If it be needful than splente it with leather /
bind it with a band of lynnen clothe after the greatness of the membre / and
bind it stetly that it meile not in no side / that the band hold it fast /
but take heed thereto that ye fast byndynge make not ill accidence. The iii.
manner. is the bloody uyng and laxatyre if it be need / and a good diela in the
beginning to the time till the pain and imposin macyon is driven away / than
shall ye dieta be stronger / as I have aforesay deu^ the lix. chap. and that
thereto come no yl^ accidete / than shall the first byndynge be styll un to the.
x. day. And some other leave it to the v. or. vii. day. and in the end shall
th^ bre be made strong with sedynge or (...) singe of roses / and worwood /
and with a Chyreclothe / or with oxcierato / ye mebre shall be brought again in
his first stregthe and workynge. The. iiij. manner is. as there is evil
accidetes / payne / or i^ol^u macion / that it may be driven away or the
dislocacie be set in again / for much handelynge it is to fere coming thereto
ye cramp or other accydentes / and it shall be done with woll depte in warm water
/ and lynseede oil / than it be brought to his first nature (as Albucasis
saith) Is the dyslocacyon with a wound / than shall ye shortly it set in
again / and cure ye wound / and if it ^e dyth sow the wound / and there
shall be let on the wound a hole open for clensyng out the matter. Is the
dyslocacie with a fracture / than dress first the dyslocacie and tha the
fracture / is it possible. If it be not possible do the contrary. Is the
dismembrynge out / is there hardness / than must ye bathe it as is aforesaid. and
salve it (...) dial thea / and plaster it with dyaquilo magno / kemdewolle
deped in mustilaginibus / yt is the slyme of papple / lynseed / fenigreke /
roots of the papple sodden / and stamped with grese / and as the place is well
wekyd than pull the membre inagayn / and bind it as I have said before.

Of the dyslocacie of the Jawbone. Ca. lxxviij.
OF this dismembryng of the Jawbone is in. ii. manners. The one / as it gothe
forward out of the joint / than bids the mouth open. The other. as it is
behind / than comes the upper most teeth over the undermost / tha ye can not
open the mouth. The tokes of this dislocacie without the common tokens is / that
the tethes come not like on the other. And if it not hastily is setin again /
it will be hard and brengeth axcys / payne / and ill acci^t and doth the
parsone dye within. x. days. (as Auice. and Haly abbas saith) As the
dislocacie happens behyndewarde / tha it shall thus be setin again. The
servant must hold the heed of the patient / than put your thombe in his mouth
well behind / your other fingers under the cheke / and threst (...) your
thombe downward / strongely pulling to you / lift up with your fyngers that
it may come in / thereafter salve it with dyaithea. Is the dislocacie before /
than lays Wylthelm? and Lanfrancus a strong band under the chyne which
may keep ye hole chyne / and a small stycke as deep in his mouth as it may be
done / than they pulls the ends of the band styfly upward / and hold the
knee on the pacyent. And the patient must lye high with the shulders (as
Jameric{is} saith) so shall it be brought in by the grace of god. Than lay
thereon this plaster following.

A Plaster.
Take Brenmeel. xii. ounces. Dragantum Gommi arabici / ^astick / Bolus armen^.
of each ij. ouces. this drive to gyder in powder / and mydle them with the
white of eggs / stryke it on a clothe / lay it the ron. Than wind it about
(...) abande / dress it every two days onys. And it is would to be made fast
in. xiij. days / or there about. Lay the pacyent on a styfe heed pyllow. He
shall ete soppys / pap / yt them need not to chaw If it hath be lunge time
out of the joint / is it become harde / than shall ye bathe it (...) warm
water / and oil / and with other coueniently things / as I have learned before
in ye next chapt. than shall it turn again in his place. Comes thereto any
ill accydent / tha help him as it nedith / against the payne shere of his
here. And salve the heed with warm oil of roses behind the eerys / and
behind in the neck / and under the arm of the patient.

Of the dysmenbrynge of the neck and rygbone. Ca. lxxix.
Sometime is the dysmebrynge of ye rydgbone outward / sometime inward / sometime
beside / and sometime in ye uttermost spodyles of ye rydgbone and it makes
Squinansie / that is with a bult before / sometimes is the dysmebrynge in the
vndermoost part / or spondyles / sometimes in that myddyl / than makes a bult
on ye bake / the token of ye dysmebrynge shall be known by the sight / and by
the feeling It is said that all this dysmebrynge of the spondyles / or backbone
/ is sore peryllous and ill to set in again for the synewes / and the back mary
/ or nucha / and most as the dyslocacie is inward / for it may not be
hadeleth / the dyslocacie of ye vppermoost spodyles that doth harm to
swellowe in the meet drink / the myddellest doth harm to the brethe / the
vndermoost doth harm to the draught going / all times ye dyslocacie is
dredefull in what place she is / the first spodyles of the neck is sore bound
with synewes / on the bones of ye heed / and therefore it is great peryl / and
between the last bone of the neck / yt is the. vii. the. viij. spodyles / it
is the first there the rybbes have his beginning / by twene them it is great
peril for ye meuyng of the neck / and therefore in the same. ii. places of the
spondyles or back bone thercometh sonner ye dyslocacye than in any other / and
his dyslocacye is sore peril. The dyslocacye that is in the vppermoost
spondyles that is cutting of ye neck / that causes ye death hastily of a man
for cause that ye inthrestynge bone stops the wind / and takes away his
life / as this dyslocacye is between ye. vij. and. viij spondyles / than is the
way stops of the meet and drink / and the way of the air is thouched / and
as the dyslocacye is under ye viij. spondyle / than leases the nether most
members his meuynge / for the stoppynge / and hurtynge of the synnewes and
nucha / whereof comes all time the meuynge and feeling / Therefore it is
needful shortly it tobe setin again / and as the bone in ye neck is out of
the joint / than hangs the heed forward / or behyndeward / and the pacyet
cannot speak / and them shall you help thus Je shall have a seruaunt to hold
the pacyet with one hand under the chyne / the other hand on the heed / and
let him hold fast / than set your hand on ye pacyent on his neck and command
the servant that he the heed hold up ward / ye shall with your hand threst
downward unto ye time till ye have set in again the bones of the pacyent / is
ye first spodyle out the joint / is it not shortly set in again tha shall he
dye / And in this manner following shall it be set in again (as Albuca. Haly abbas
/ Auicenna / Lancfrankcus saith) that heed shall wise pulls with ye hands /
and with one ^ bind / lay him a small styke in the mouth and threst him upward
by the chyne / or with the here / up by the eerys / the shoulder shall be threst
downward with the feet / and he shall be pulls in both places with good
provision / with cords or other instrumetes when the. vii. back bone or
spendyle is out ye joint of ye. viij. spodile tha tarry not long of ye
insettynge / and gothe ye dyslocacye inward / than kills the parsone shortly
/ he is seldom helped / nevertheless begyne the cure / and threst him the
shoulder down. ward / and pull the neck as is a fore said / Is ye dyslocacie
outward / that seldom happeth / that may be help with ye hand strongely to
threst downward as ye best can / with stretchynge of the neck / and with neder
threstynge the shoulder downward.

Is the dismembrynge benethe the. viij. spondyle and y^ it gothe sore inward
than it is deedly / and it shall never be hol^e / is it not hole ^ward / but
that it lonely threst the ^ucha / than the nethermost members lyseth his
meuynge. As the dislocacie is inward / than there byded at every time a bulte
how well it be cures / nevertheless theris a cure of the spondyles / whereof
grows a cro^ed back / and that shall be threstin with youchade in ye best manner
as it can be done or with a board that thereto is made. Whaye have ho^pe them /
than bind there upon this pla^ter here after following.

A Plaster.
Take Dyle o^ roses. iij. ous. Mumie Ma^tick Bolyarmen^ / Dragantum Myrt^llo
ruin / Gomi arabici / ofeche. ii. ouc. mydle it to gyder with the white of
eggs in the manner that it be thynne / and depeth therein clothes and they lay
there upon / and there over lay. ii. splentes made with tow and depte in the
^ame. than bind him softly. There (...) ^ethym blood on the hand / and make
him going to the draught. and he shall ete ^ made with eggs with crommes of ^
de depte in barley water. And he shall dr^ke water wherein is sod Cheryses or
bac. y. And dress him at every. v. days ^ / the patient shall be laid upward
that the ^morynge may be threst down. And the time of his helynge is. xx.
days.

Of the dyslocacyon of therybbes. Ca. lxxx.
^S the rybbes be out the joint / than right it set it in with the hand lay
there over ye aforesaid plaster dep^e in (...) white of eg. wrynge it out again
/ but it shall first be dept in water wrynge it out. therouer bind. ii.
splentes not to last / So bind him. ix. days loge. all times lay thereon the
defensiuu. and rule him (...) meet and drink as is aforsayd. If in this place
comany oneuen knoddes / tha salve him every day (...) the salve made of Oil.
xii. ouc. Wax / Fenigrekemeele of ech^. ii. ou. Rosyll. vi. ou. Butter. iiij.
ou. Frakensens Bdellij / of each an ove. Ducks grese / K^pons grese / of each
an ouc. mydle this together on the fire salve the place therewith And ye shall
know that this Salve takyth away ye knoddys of the members / and makes even /
and set the bo^ys right.

Of the dyslocacie of the bonys of the shulders. Ca. lxxxi.
THis bone comes not hole out ye joint / but that bone de^a^teth somewhat out
his place (...) than shall ye help ye bone (...) your hand there over ye
a^orsayde plaster / And lay there ou^ small (...) shyns of five to we / and
thereafter splentes every day the desen ^ him blood going to the drawght and
rule him u^ mete and drink as is aforsayd. Is there a woude sow them / lay
thereon this powder of Mastick Dragos blood / Gomi arabici / Dragantu / of each.
ii. ou^. Thereafter cleanse the wound (...) this plaster. ix. days lunge.
Take^ose honey. xii. ouc. (...) meel / or barley meel / or mylst^ meele. iii^.
ouc. frakensence / aloes / of each an ouc. as the woude is clensyd / tha heal
it (...) the ^am^ powder. or with the gren^ wooded plaster. or (...) both. And
his mete drink shall be as I have said oftentimes before.

Of the dysmenbrynge of the shulders. Ca. lxxxij
AUicena set alone. ii. manners in this dismebrynge. Albucasis and other
masters saith that there be more in the should{er} / for it gothe out ye ^oxce
of ye shoulder in. iij. manners. The first / that the heed of ^habone of the
vppermoost arm separteth downward. The other comes foreward to the first
part. The. iij. in ye midst upward / but backward can it not come out the
shoulder bone. The first dysmebrynge is be know^ by ye sight ^elynge as th^r is
feled ye heed of the arm pipe vnd the hole of the arm / and upon the shoulder
is seen an holnes. The other dysmebrynge is know by the ^inge of the heed of
the arm^ype before ^ se an holnes Th^hyrde is in the midst vpwart / is to
kn^we / as the patient cannot retche out his ellebow from his body vnd ye arm
ye se an ^olnes / and on the shu^ an hyghnes.

The manner for to set it in again is this Is i^chylde (...) a ^ge parson^
that shulderbone is out of the toynte / than take it (...) your ^este han^ and
make a fist with your right hand / set it so v^ the holl of the arm upon ye ^
than lift ^ de with your fist like if it hang on any thing / than comes
the bone in his right place: The other manner is / as ye patient is old great
/ and ^ him not list up / than command ^to lye on his back / then shall ye
(...) roud bowl of tree / wind it about (...) clothes lay it under the holl
of his a^me on the out coming bone / than shall ye treed (...) your heel on
the roud bowl stefly downward / and take the patient (...) the hand and
p^llestefly downward / than comes the arm again in his ryghteplace. The.
iij. manner is. the patient shall be pulls (...) the arm over a staff / in ye
midst of the staff a bowl woude about (...) clothes / both the ends of the
staf shall be made fast hyer tha ye length of a man. And the paciet shall stade
upon a stole / than shall ye pull ye arm over the staf / tha shall ye also
push ye stole f^om under his sot / so shall the bone be (...) by ye grace of
god. The. iiij. manner is wa^ad der / in the same manner as you have done (...)
ye staf (as Haly abbas / A louca^ ^. Brun^ saith) But Roger^ please better that
Guydo saith (...) the foot / with ye ^ with ^he staf / not with the ladder. The
syfte ^aner is with the instrument as ^ death in picture / and in all manner as ^
by the same pycture. And the dismembr^ be setin also with retchynge and
pulling and with threstynge in with the hade or (...) a clothe (as Lank^
saith) And will it notbe setin again / for cause that it has the lunge ben
out of the joint / is bec^ harde / than shall ye wasshe it with warm water /
as is asoresayd / and make it soft brenge it in again. And as it is done than
pleases me Rogeri^ / ye which in the first iij. days dresses the paciet
with a ^ (...) clothe and tow depte in whyt or eggs Thereafter with ye plaster
of mylstufm^ele dragons blode. c. as I have said before. And ye shall lay under
the arm of the patient a bowl with clothes / or made of tow and byndehym
well fast with a band that is. v. fyngers broad / as loge as it nedyth.



Of the dysmenbrynge of the elbow. Ca. lxxxiij.
THis dislocatio of ye elbow as (Auicenna saith) is sometimes great / sometimes
small / Albuca. other masters saith yt it gothe sometimes forward out the joint
/ and sometime be hynde / The token of this dysmembrynge is heuynes in ye
meuynge / that it is not possible the pacyent to bring the hand to ye shoulder
/ The elbow comes heuely out ye joint is heuely to set in again / for thesene
was daynes. Of the setting in and cure saith Auicenna that it is i^. ii.
manners / the first with the any hand hold the shoulder / with ye other hand to
drive in it again that is out / with styff detynge behind on the elbow / with a
salved hand with oil / till it comes in again / Rogerius saith the manner of
bin dynge / Lanca^rcancus set the cure thereof with stretchynge with vphanggynge /
or with berynge or weight / if the dyslocacio gothe forward or behind ward /
but Guydo set it in with the knee as dyslocacie is forward. is dyslocacio it
afterward or behind so set he it in the hand (as Auicenna writes) the manner
of the insettynge with the knee or heel that shall be done in it that is
forward Je shall take a broad longhande about his arm / yt the. ii. end goo
behind let your seruaunt hold both ye ends in every hand one / and the
pacyent shall be bound on his foot / and shall be hold / and command the
pacyent to stretch out his arm / tha command the servant with the hand to
pull backward / than shall the master hastily the arm set foremarde to senn
the shoulder again. Tha threst in with the knee that there stand outward /
brenge the arm to the shoulder. As it is out behind / tha is good ye arm to
be bowed / ouertwart by a little lift up the arm / turn it somewhat (as Ja
meric{is} saith) In ye fastmakinge of this cur^ follow all things as I have
learned in the aforesaid chaptre / but the arm shall be berynge about the neck
/ by little and lytyl shall he be bound higher / till the hand come to the
shoulder / and every. iiii. day shall it be dresses onys. And at every time
shall be bowen the membre. And it is woute to be healed in. xv. days.

Of the dysmenbrynge of the hand or knot of the wrest. Ca. lxxxiiij.
THe bone of ye hand goth lightly out of the joint / is lightly to setin again
/ as it be (...) quykly. And as it bydeth^ time out of the joint / than com
thereto sometime an ipostumacion / and than it is with great payne heuynes to set
it in again. And this dismebrynge is most before or behind. the cure thereof
shall be done with stretching / pulling / and meuyng with downward thressynge.
But I take the lift hand of the paciet in my hand stetly by the knot / take
his myddell finger in my right hand. stretchynge and pulling the same finger
/ in the pulling threst I on the outcomyng theragaynst / with the finger under /
or with the thombe above / so it will lyghtely be setin. In the fast making is
none other cure tha I have learned you And Jameric{is} healed this in. xii.
days. Is there a woude / than bind him yt the woude may besene en every day.

Of the dysmenbynge of the fyngers. Ca. lxxxv.
THe dismembrynge of the fyngers that comes lightly and is lightly set in / if
he be brusyd than help him thus stretch ye finger as I have learned in the
next chapytre / lay thereon this plaster following.

A plaster.
Take been meell / orote meell. xii. ounces / mastyck / dragantum / gum of
Arabie of each an ounce / make thereof a soft plaster with the white of eggs /
and lay it thereon and bind it there about / and let it be boude unto ye.
iiij. day / and bind him again till he be hole.

Of the dsymenbrynge of the bonys of the hyppys. Ca. lxxxvi.
A^ice. saith as this dysmembrynge of ye hyppes is inward forward / than the
leg is longer than otherwise / and the pacyent steps up the hole fete /
and he may not bow forward / that heed of ye thyghe is gone inward in the
lyske / and in ye vterpt is holownes In ye dysmebryng afterward and outward
causes the leg be ye short / and the patient may not set his heel on the
ground / The cure thereof lerneth Albucasis / and is sore {pro}fytable to all
manners and ye shall the syke fast hold by ye shulders or he shall be bound
over the shulders on ye thyghe / with a band on a wyndas / and the other band a
bow ye knee on the same wyndas / than pull the membre out with the wind / with
the hade right it till it be set in / The first dysmembrynge wyche is inward
before shall the pacyent be puleth / with the foot or knee drive it in again
As the dysmembryng is outward and behind / so shall ye pacyent in like wise be
pull that the heyth with ye kne be threst inward and the holnes may come out /
and for this dysmembrynge lightly to set in again / so must ye have a table
longer than the pacyet and make on every end a wind / and in the midst under
the back and on ye belly shall the pacyent be bound on the wind with a lunge
towel / and with an other shall be bound on the knee / and wind about ye whole
pipe with the towel unto the foot / and shall be bound so on the other wind
and than shall ye wind with both the wyndas to gyder and set that bone of the
pacyent in again / and than the byndynge of this shall be like as it stand
before in that chapytre of dysmebrynge from the uppermost arm of the adiutorium
/ but it shall be bound faster.

Of the dysmenbrynge of the knee shynes. Ca. lxxxvij.
AS these dysmembrynge is done / than shall ye comaude the pacy^ to stand up
on both his feetes / hold him his place / and thereafter bind it with a
plaster of sycer meele of been meele like as I have learned you / and dress
him all. iiij. days onys / Is there a woude so do as I have before learned you /
with byndyng / with defensiuum / with blood letting / and with meet and drink c.

Of the dysmembrynge of the knees, Ca, lxxxviij.
AL so ye shall know that ye knees comes lightly out the mebre / and is
lightly to set in again / It goothe often times again in / so soon as ye
pacyent stepped on ye feet / If it goo not so in again / tha shall the surgean
have one servant / wiche shall pull the leg / in ye time that he pulls shall
ye set in again the kne Tha lay therouer a clothe dept in rose oil / and on
that clothe lay the plaster of Been meel / and Dragons blood / as I have said
often times before / There over shall ye bind with one lunge band / and thyn
plumacioles of tow dept in the white of eggs / like stands in the. lix:
chapytre / and there over bind / as is a ^rsayd / Is there a woude it shall be
bound that it may be seen every day / Also may ye the dyslocacyon and
dysmembryng of the knee and anclowe lightly set in again with a wind / like
the pycture here after following shows.

Here after foloweht an instrument in pycture for the knee or anclo we lightly
to set i^ again that is out of the joint



Of the dysmembrynge of the feet. Ca. lxxxix.
THe dysmenbryng of the feet is suddenly done / shortly setin again / and it
is heuely to make fast / for the many bonys yt the joint makyth / The token
thereof is the hyghnes of the but coming bone and the payne and leasing of the
meuynge / right this bonys set it in as even like as ye can / ye may not that
membre to much stretch / of such strong stretching should come so much
payne / that thereof should come an impostumacion / therefore ye shall the feet
softly stretch her and there turnynge / and with the other hand shall ye ye
heyghnes threstin again / till it may come in his right place / and as it is
made even / than wind roundabout the foot a clothe that well dept in warm
rose oil / that strength the veins and takyth away the payne. Over the
clothe lay the plaster of been meell and dragos blode / as is written in the
chaptre of the insettynge of ye leg. than salve the leg with that ^stuum as
there comes no impostumacio to / and over the plaster shall ye lay plumacyoles
of tow ^nd there over splynttes / the rafter shall ye bind the feet well / and
lay the foot hye / so that the leg may the better defend from the impostumacio
/ ye shall dres him. iiij. or. v days but ones / ye shall hold ye foot. xxx.
or. xl. days lunge in rest.

Of the dysmebringe of the bone on the feet. Ca. ^x
SEt this membre in again in his rygt place / than lay there over ye plaster /
of cycer meele or rye meel. xij. ouc. dragons blode / mastick / dragantum g^n^
ara^ / of each. ii. ouc. boly armeni / mumie / of each an osic. this mydle to
gyder with the white of eggs. tha bind him but not to fast. And salve the foot
with defensiuu / And salve him at last with dyalthea / there over one oxierociu.
Ite is there a shoulder. hyppe / leg / knee / or foot out of the joint is
become harde / for the lunge being out of the joint. And will you it letin
again tha take lynseed / dowys downgh / make it clean ^rom straw / chyppe /
(...) / see the it well with gotys me^ke in a pot / and stryke it on a cloth /
lay it on the membre / and it shall be so^te in. iiij. hours. than set wisely
the mebre again in his place with ^y of the instrumetes that best serves to
(...) membre as it stands in picture. of ^ ked leg after the xix. chaptre.
of ye ^ arm after the. xviij. chaptre. of the ^oked knee after. lxxij.
chaptre. and will the joint or membre abide to soft / than make a clote wet in
rynnynge water and wrapit about the joint or membre / it will make it ^ast
again.

Of the harde styf and crooked membrys how and in what manner they shall be cured
or / helpen / and ryghted. Ca. xci.
IT happens sometime that after ye helynge of a wooded joint or membre that it
abides crooked / styff / or hard / than shall ye the membre or joint bathe
saftmakyng with old oil / and with water yt is meetely warm like melke war
me that is first molkeu / and bathe the membre with a great sponge / and
thereafter shall ye bathe that membre with papple and hye mallowe roots. v. or.
vi. days / thereafter take any of ye a fore set conterfayte instrumetes / as
the instrument of a crooked arm stadynge after the. xviij. chap. or the
instrument of the crooked leg after the. xix. chap. standing. or the instrument
of the crooked knee stadynge after ye. lxxij. chaptre. of this istrumentes take
yt you serves best for ye mebre. And stretch therewith every day a little
Thereafter salve it with the salve following after this after written bathing /
and this bathing make thus / Ye shall seethe ye heed feetes of a gilded wedder
/ there with bathe the membre And if it not there with amede tha wet a clothe in
the same sop lay it about ye mebre bathe it there with / Or take a great sponge
wet in the same sop lay it warm there on. And so oft as ye the membre bathe
/ or lay thereon the clothe / or ye sponge / so often make a fire of saw
duystmeel thereby let dry ye arm or leg. as the mebre is dried / than salve
it by the fire of the saw meell with this salve of hogs grese / gray grese /
of each. viij. onc. kapos grese / ye mary of a calf / fresshe butter / oliu
nucis iuda ice / oliu sysamini / oil of sweet almons / ^i me of hye malowes /
slyme of lynseed / slyme of fenygreke. iiij. ouces. storacis calamite / bdellij
gumi / ysopi humide / of each anouc. the grese melt / it may not touche salt
/ as it is melted than do therein the oils and the slymes / and make thereof a
salve.

An other good safte making.
Sethe lynseed /. xij. figs. tha take sour dowgh /. ii. roasted oynonus.
musterdseed doves donge / barley meele / of each like much / that stamp al to
gyder in a mortar th^ do thereto a little oil olyue tha it shall be a plaster and
lay it there upon.

These plaster is also good to all swerynge and impostumacyon. And can he not
go to the draught in this fykenes / tha make this bathe of papple / water^res
or genacio in latyne / parydane / edera achorea / camomyll flowers / of each an
hadefull / this do al to gyder in a little lyne bag seethe it in water / in
ye water shall ye paciet him bache to the nauyll. so goth the swerynge away
through the draught going through the vryne. And if it goth so away / than
sees barley in water do therein a little honey and give it the patient to drink
/ than shall the place inwardely be clensyth.

Howe the cosumynge mebres ought to be helped and cured. Ca. xcii.
WIth a woollen clothe and with water of the styngynge nettylles shall ye first
(...) be ye membre or joint. (...). or. iiij. days / every day ii. or. iij.
times. The second ye shall set ventoses or boxes about the sore / and take
them of again / yt shall ye do. iii. or. iiij. days lunge without pryckynge.
The. iij. if he have in the joint great payne / than shall ye make him this
water. Take the liver / ye hart / and the longues of a black calffe there with
chap sage. ii handful / and mengle it with ye same c^es blood that it may be
moysty therewith / do it in a still a tory which is called alembicu and
dystylle water therout / therewith was she ye mebre every day. iij. or. iiij.
times yt shall help him. The. iiij. when ye have done this before said / than set
him in a bathe stew ^et on him the ventose or box / and garsse him / but set
the ventose no more upon and anoint ye garssynge all the membre with this salve
following.

A Salve.
Take aqua vite / (...) eu^or^ / long pepper made all in powder mydle them to
gyder that they be not to thycke / afterward lay this plaster on ye sore /
give him every day a fresshe plaster.

Another good plaster to the same.
Take creffysshes stamp they with ye shell les all the body / than stryke it on
a blew woollen clothe and lay it on the joint / where by the joint shall be come
full of blaynes / salve the joint with the before said salve / and this plaster
is shortly ^ole stynking / therefore ye must lay thereon in. i^. days onys a
fresshe plaster again.

Another proved experiment to the same.
Bind about that membre there it is consumed a roope of here / and let it lye
thereon as lunge as he may suffer it. that do at the le^ iij. or. iiij. times
in. iij. days. And afterward set him in a bathe stew / set over ^ll the
place there it is consumed ventoses or bores and let them styll hang thereon /
and when ye take them of / tha set them no more upon. anoynte him with the sa^e
following.

A Salve.
Take vnguet^ a grippe / arago / ^iato of each. viij. ouces. castorye oil /
mustart sede oil / of each. i^. ouc. (...) oil. vi. ouc. oliu lauti. iii^.
ouc. dogs grese. ii. ouc. put all these to gyder in a pan on the fire and
styre them well / and do therein this powder of lunge pepper / euforbium / of each
an ouce. white mustartse de / half an o^e. and than put thereto aqua vite that
it be not to thick / let it set together / salve him

This salve following shall be take last to the consumed members.
Stape the roots herb of wild sanicle or dia^esie agrestis in latin in the
month of may / with may butter / let them stand ii^. days lunge. than sethe
it softly over the fire / strayn it again through a clothe this makes to
grow flesh and blood.

A sereclothe after yt the membre is brought in his first form
Take wax. iiij. ouces / whyt rosel / mastick / armoniacu / of each an ounce /
oil of castory / oil of camomylle of each half an ouce / worwode (or
absintium in latin) feni greek / comyn of lombardie / of each a dragma /
vynegre. viij. ounces. And make it in powder that shall be powdret / and mydle
it together / and make thereof a plaster.

A fair conynge to this same
Do a small kettle full of warm w^ a crane as the barbours occupy / and
(...) it a manys length high or higher over the pacyent / and the pacyent
shall sit under the said kettle / he shall lay that consuming mebre in a basin
/ or in a payl / or in an other vessel / so as ye place be not wet there he
shall sit / and the crane shall be turned that it may drop a little out drop
by drop following and falling / on that ^onsumynge membre / and of the same
dropping comes the blood in ye same place there as ye warm water falls on
the membre / and ye warmnes comes in that mebre / and that is called an
embricacie / Thereafter salve that mebre with ye aforesaid salve / and lay
theren a warm plaster.

An expert plaster serving to the same.
Take white rosyl / turpetyn / black pitch melt the to gyder / do thereto
alytell Mumie as ye think best / after ye will make little or much / stryke
that on a clothe of cotton / lay ye plaster on yt membre. This plaster shall
not lye thereon but iii. hours / for it draws the blode strougely to him.

Therefore ye shall oft change ye plaster / And as often as ye will change it
tha warm it in a small pot / lay it thereon again Or ye say on the plaster / ye
shall ye aforesaid salve set in a small pot by the fire / tha warm your hand
the salve / rub the arm or other mebres therwt / after warm ye plaster on
ye fire do it so warm about the arm / than ye arm amendyth / Ye may also
occupy in all manner the water of the calves liver in like wise as the salve /
also warm / tha it is good / of this plaster ye shall wounder se. I should
write how the mebre shulde be beat with rods or nettels / like ye como barbours
do / but I have scene little profit coming thereof / therefore I will not write
of it. But I take in my beginning for the rods net tells nettyll water ^a blew
wolle cloth and rub the mebre therwt as is aforesaid in this chap. that I
here write have my self occupied / ye last medesynes ben ye strongest.

For veins shronke after ye helynge (...) Take ye bladd with ye vryne of a wild
hog in the bladder do some of his grese hanging it in ye son. xii. days
lunge or more / tha comes thereof a salve / there with anoint yt mebre.

Another Salve
Take black soope. iiij. ouces. iiij. yolks of eggs / rotes of white lylyes
clenne stapeth iiij. ouc. netes feet oil / styre it together an hour loge or
more / therwt salve yt membre there the dysseas is by ye fire / it shall amend

How you shall stauce blode / and consume it that is come with a fall or stricken
with a blonte wepyn as with a clobbe or staff or other instrument not edged /
nor cuttynge. Ca. xciij.
IN the beginning as one hath fallen / or is dredyng that the blode is engelyd
and clouted to gyder / tha let him shortly blode on the next place of the
hurting / tha make this powd

A Powder.
Take terre sigillate / mumie / boli armeni / of each an ouce. thereof give him
every day in the morning. v. or. vii. days lunge: one dragma. ^u. out. of
plateyn water / yt makes departing of the engelyd blood / stops the veins
where it comes out. will ye yt the engeled blode depart. give him of this
powder following every time a dragma. with. (...). o^ the ruell water or Cerifol^
latin. Take sperma ^ri. iii. dragma. ^mie an ofice. terre sigillate / boli a^ /
of each half an ouce. If ye will yt it shall go out through his water / tha do
thereto yt er^ of k^yffysshes half an ou. Hecht kyffel one dragma. If ye will
yt it go through the draught going / than (...) out the powder of bol
^rmen{is} and terra sigillata. do there to reba^ half an out: that drives ^t
the engeled b^de through the draught going. And if ye patient be pore may not
paye th^or / than take for ye ^ber sterre be muris half an once / and give him
half a dragma ^che evil (...) more bery water / at every time an once / lewke
warm.

As a parsone hath engeled blood in the maw / or in ye guts / so let him
make this pylles / If he be strong / so give it him at ones / If he be feeble
than give it him at twyes Take Rebarbere one dragma. Mumie. vi. barley corns
heavy. and make thereof pills with wine. If ye have not this / or if he be a pore
man / than give him black coals of elm wode / eyes of kreeffysshe / leues of
charuyll dried / or cerifoltu in latin. of each like much / make thereof a
powder / give the patient thereof half an ouce with a little vynegre. or give him
ground worms stapt wiht oak coals mydled with vinegre / strain it through a
clothe / do thereto Rube tine toru dried. iiij. barley corns heavy.

Howe you shall help him or them that thrughe such a fall / stroke / or
chaunche / be faint or feole. Ca. xciiij.
THe parsone that is beten or fallen / has thereof a stoppyng in the breast of
the moystnes after following / which gothe forth to the inward payne

As such paciet is let blode / the blode is stopped and driven out / then
shall ye give him this recepte following.

One recepte.
Give him Syropi violaru / Dragagan tu frigidu. Lolac de papauere / Succer
penidiaru / of this he shall aete at marowe ateuenyng / at every time a dragma
/ This recepte shall be made at the appottecaris / is wrythen thus. Recipe
specieru electua{rum} degumis sieve species a dragma / specierum diadragatu
frigidum. ii. dragma. manus chrysticu perlis. vi. dragma. sirupi viola{rum} a
dragma. succer penidiarum. iij. dragma.

If any man be fall or brusyd whereby he perbraketh / the meet yt he takes
may not abide in him / than give him to drink in the morning and evening
Siruyi citoni oru. and anoynte the maw without with oil mirtillo{rum} / with
oil macis. straw over the oynteme ye powder of reed coral or give him sugar
of violet an ouce temperyd with bolo armeno. xx. barley corns heavy with this
syrupe hereafter write / made with herttong levies or foliss scholopendre in latin
/ plane teynleuys / of each an ouce. sod in a quart of water till it be halue
consumed / tha strain it / put thereto sugar. iiij. ouc. white lylye water.
iij. ouc. scabiose water. ii. ouces this syrupe makes the breast rum large

If any parson have fall whereby much blood is spylte the parsone sore febled.

A powder for to drink
Take yelowe eyestone / bol^ armen^ / balaus^e / sanguis draconis / Lacca / of
e^ much / made all in powder / grue i^ cyent to drink. iii. dragma of ye same
(...) ^der with water wherein is soden sumac. x. ^a^ly corns heavy. This medesyn
stops soon the blode / cosumeth it hastily as the patient takes meet which
stops.

Howe you shall helpen him that is fallen or betyn / and if his blode be run /
or engeled like cruddys / the flesh brusyd. Ca. xcv.
HEre shall ye learn to defend to make last the place yt is hurt / that there
come no ipostume / nor swelling / nor other evil accident. The first. as one
is fallen from an high place / or sore beten / yt he hath lost his spece / or
yt he hath his spece but speaks folyshly / than is in doughte that ye brain
the members of the heed be perysshyd.

And Auicenna saith the wit of vnderstadynge showyth the helte of the brain
/ yet it is needly to search / if he be deed or alive / which ye shall know by
feeling the pulse / calling him / pulling him by the eeres / and take fine tow
/ or kemyd wolle / and hold it at his mouth / before his nose holys and so
shall ye see if the wind come out or not / and if ye see one good token yt the
breest steryth any thing / than make him to nese with pepper / euforbio / and
rub his members with vynegre / and with herb a grace and make him blede with
the nesynge / and as he is come by one manner to him self / tha let him blood /
and glitter him as I have le^ed you. If the patient be hurt in the brain /
than follow ye learning of the bruising / or contusion of the heed / but if ye
hole body be brusyd or hurt / than anoynte all ye hurt place with oil of
roses / or with oil myrtyllorum / and straw therouer ye powder of myrtyll /
as is a fore said of the woudes with the brusynge / Some lays such a paciet
in warm horse dounhe / lets him therein sweet / and yt helps him / but
Haliabbas / and Auicenna binds him in a shepes skin that is fresh and
warm / yt is ^leene anon / and straw yt with a little beten or stampte salt
/ let him lye therein a hole day / and the other day he shall be hole. In the
out pulling of the blood the work masters hath wrought after ye counsel of
Hali abbas / the place shall be made strounge with a clothe depte in cold water
and lay thereon / but I was wounte to do in that water much salt and wta blew
wolle cloth / that I first and often laid on yt membre / for it consumyth the
engelyd blode / and makes the place fast / and as he is strong than make the
body to sweet with hot ger

And if it help not / tha consume it in this manner hereafter write / it softeth
the payne of the engeled blood / opens ye swetynge holes.

A Salve.
Take dial thea. ii. ouces / holy armeni one ouce / oliu myrtylloru / oil of
comomylle oil of roses / oil of dylle / of each. iii. ounces / myrtylle in
powder. ii. ouces / wa^i dragma melt these together / and than do ye powder
therein / and there with shall ye same or anoint ye pacyent / in like wise doth
this medesin / that is often proved in the shoal of bonome / pryncypally on him
that is be^n and ye strokes be not deep / than take a sheep skin warm from
ye sheep / straw there on salt made in small powder. ii. {per}tes. ky^s seed in
powder one part / lay the (...) (...) warm on his body. And for the con^me
that engeled blod. Take venys soope small cut. iiij. ounces / vnguentum dyal
thea^. ounces / melted together / and there with salve or anoint the pacyent at
morning and evening / and if the stroke be great that ye skin is swollen /
than cut the skin open / and draw that blood out / than heal it as another
wound.

Adrynke that heleth ye flesh win under the skin / doth de{per}te ye
engeled blood.

Take Sarcocolle albe one dragma / sumac. ii. dragma. alume cisi one dragma.
rubetinctorum. xl. barley corns heavy, planteyn water and wine wherein is soden
mastick of each. xii. ouces / honey. vi. ounces meddle these together / and give
the ^acyet (...) drink every morning ^stynge / and late at evening / at
every time. iii. ouces. If there be one sore fall / or beten on his back and
there is nothing broken nor no membre out of joint / un the hath great payne
/ than take. iii. boss^elles of bran / and seth it in a ketell with water / and
styre it well till the bran be meetly dry / and put thereto a certain part
of butter / or creme / and sethe that meetly dry / and do it in a kymeell /
and lay the patient therein on his back as hot as he may suffer it / and as
it begin wax cold tha do thereto more out of the ketel. this do at morning
/ at none time / at evening / and at every time as he comes therout and is
dry / tha salve him rub him with vnguentum dyalthea that may suck thrugh ye
skin / and it were good to do thereto walt rothe (or abra in latin) And there
is nothing better as a mebre is hurt or fallen yt ye take in the beginning
hemp seed well stamped and a little water thereto And if the water ware of the
herb named storckes bylle (or herba rubea in latin) it were very good to lay
that on ye hurt place ii. fyngers thycke between. ij. clothes / and at every
time as it is dry / than lay thereon another / that heleth without payne. As
any is beten in his face that it is blew / tha stryke ye blew place. (...).
or. iii. times with yt sap of ye rote of wild sa^a / or cartam{is} latin or
take sap of sigillu salomonis one dragma / vnguentu albu one ouce / the white
of eggs half anounce / al this mydle together and stryke ye blew place there
with at morning / at none and at evening.

Here ends the virtuous hand work of surgery.
Here after follows the Antidotharius in the which thou may learn howe thou
shalt make many and divers noble plasters / salves / powders / oils / and
wound drynkes / the which be very necessary and (...) hove full / vtyll / and
profytable for every surgeon therein to be expert / and ready at all times of
need.


One apostolicum salve.
IN the first make an Apostolicum Salve after the Antithodario Nycolay.

Take Litargiriu. xii. ouuces. gtekes pytche rede wax / of each. iiii. ouces
oak mystyndyn / whyt wax of each. ij. ouces. are moniacu / magnete stone which
is called ye lead stone / of each an onc. an half. Sarco coll / Squama eris /
Dyptan / Aristologia longa / Spanysshe grene / Appoponatu of each. ii^. dragma.
white Frankensen^e / mastyk / of each. i^. ouces / turpentyne / gal banu /
bdelliu / myrra / brent coper / of each ii^. dragma / that litargirium shall ye
stam pe in powder / and thereto do vii^. ounces of oil olyue / and let it sede
together on ye fire that it be thycke as wax / and that shall ye drop on a
stone / in a prove / than do thereto the turpentyne / that white and rede wax /
as that is melted / than do therinthe galba number / appoponatum / bdellium /
sarcocolle / weked one night in vynegre / soden / strey ned / than put it
therein together / and than take it from ye fire and dotherin the gomes and as it
be wa^n^ / than shall ye do therein al the other parcels the one after the
other made in powder / and styre it till it be cold and than may ye make it in
collis.

One ep^rocium plaster.
Of this plaster wrytyth Rie^us in his anti (...) this is needful to every good
surgian. Take saffran shype ^ bytche / new wax of each vii^. (...) / ^pentyne
^al banu / armoniacum / myr^e / mastyk / white fran (...) of each. ii. ounces
and. in^ dragm^ This plaster make thus / melt the wax / ^pytche / greeks
pytche / turpentyne / melt i^ together / when yt is molten do therein galbanu /
armonilcum / one night steped in ^ynegre / sode and ^ynyd do it therein Than
shall ye fethe it again till ye vynegre be consumed / and styre it well together /
and than do therein the other parcels made in powder / styre it till it begin
to wax cold th^n cast it upon a cold stone / and ye shall anoyn^ ye stone
first woyle of bay leues (or (...) lauri in latin) and than work the s^ffran
therein / whanye have so done than may ye make colles of it.

One diaqu^on plaster.
Make this plaster after the Antithodario mos^e. Take lytargirium. xxiii^.
ounces / oil of blew lylyes / oil of camo mylles / oil of dyll (or anetum
in latin) of each. xii^. ounces / lyusedes sleme / fenegrenes sleme / hye
malowe ^otes sleme / ^leme of fyrg / sap of yrios / sap of mersybelen / the
grefe soden of the molle that hangs by (...) the legs of ye sheep / bird
lyme (or viscu^ in latin) of each. xxv. ounces / turpety^e. vi. ounces / white
rosyl / ielowe wax of each. iii^. ounces / take lytargiriu make it in powder
and dress it with ye oil ^leme and grese / that it be thycke as wax as it is
dropped upon a stone / tha do thereto that wax / rosyll / turpentyne / and as
it is molten together / than styre it together till it be cold / and thereafter
make rolls of it with oil of white lylyes.

A sereclothe plaster.
The fere clothe plaster is very good to al members that is out of the joint /
and the cosumyng mebres / or which is grieved with cold moystnes / that
consumyth and brengyth the mebre again in his right power. Take wax. vi.
ounces / rosyll. ii^. ounce mastyk. ii. ouces. armoniacum / galbanu white
frankencence of each an ounce and a hall / oil of bybergeylle (or olium
castor^ platyn) oil of camomylle of each and (...) ^greke meele / meele of
warmwode / (...) of lombart comyn / meele of camomylle stoces / made all this
in small powder of each a dragma / vynegre. v. or. vi. ounces / melt the rosyl
/ wax / and the oil together / than do therein the galbanum / and armoniacum
steped in vynegre and streyne it / and at the last do thereto the other
parcels / yt is made in small powder / and styre it well together till it be
cold.

Of the grene wooded plaster.

The good grene wounded plaster that ye new surgyans occupy / that heleth al
frysshe woudes without tents / and it is a mudificatinu a coglutinati^ and a
cosolida* ti^u / And this plaster is of many diverse manners of sodry mistress
made / some take much / rosyll / and little wax / some much wax and little
rosyll / and some take wax and rosyll like much / some take no rosyl at all /
Therefore ye shall know as ye will that this same plaster shall more heal than
cleanse like as it is nedely in the wound of the heed and in a simple woude /
there as no substance is lost / If that ye take more wax in weight so much ye
lesser take of rosyl in weight / let them twene every time in his weight / and
as ye will that it cleanse more taking to her the matter / like as a
depestytchyd woude which maked much matter / than shall you take more rosyll
tha wax / as I have said / if ye will that the plaster shall make flesh to
grow / shall serve to al woudes / which somewhat hath lost of his substance /
than take rosyl / wax of each like much / or if ye will yt it make the skin
and that the woude should close than take wax alone and no rosyll / and as in
this plaster is much / rosyl little wax than is it called a mundificatinum
and attracti^um that is clensyng / drawing out ye matter / if there be therein
much wax little rosyll / than is it called conglutinat^u / that is together
leuynge and closing of the wound / and if there be therein wax and rosyll
like much / tha is it called incar nat^ yt is flesh making in the wound Or
if there be therein wax no rosyll / tha it is called consolydatiuum / that is
helyng and skin making. And this plaster is made thus. Take resin depino
that is white rosyl / maiden wax of each two poud / ye rosyl which is clear as
turpetine dere suet of each. xii. ouc. greeks pytche. vii^ ouces / sarcocolle
small and great of each. ii^. ounces / turpentine half a pound / mastyk white
Francken^ence of each. iii^. ounce^ Dragantum / Gommi Arabici / Galban^
Armoniacum of each one ounce and shall / Storacis calamite. i^* ounces /
Storaci^ liquid. iii^. ounces / And take the sap of this herbia yt ye can
(...) (...) and great or Pyrola maioret minor / Sanicle (^ ronica mayor et
minor^ herb^ solse^ / solida minor / mode^ wax teor artemisia in latin /
gl^tay^e small great / betonica / agrimonia ^erraria / matrisilua / halderio /
^arrowor cerisolium latin / ^ageor saluia in latin / ^erbene anou^ ere / wale
rote or ambra / of this he^ take sapix. po^ide no less / but cather more /
because to each pound of the substance of this plaster be longyth full, iii.
pound sappes / That sap / white Rosyl / wax / Hertes (...) and Rosyll / and
Colo^onia / ye shall se the (...) a kettel over ye fire without flame or (...)
till two parts thereof he consumed / than do therein Turpenty^ / but the (...)
andragantu / go^ arabici / galbanu / armoniacu / this shhalbe first steped on^
night (...) vynegre of roses / as it is soden a waim^ or. ii^. tha shall ye the
other gommes make in powder / and do it therein and let it sethe again. i^. or.
iii. walmes / and at the last do therein Storaxliquida / and Calamita. if ye
will have better smelling / than do thereto besym or barot{is}. iii. ouc. /
ifye will have it very well smelling / tha do thereto. ii. or. ii^. ounces of oil
of spyke / than strain it thrugh a clothe / and let it stand a night the
next day cut this ^alue in. iii^. p^t^s / than take it out of the ketyll /
make thereof rolls with fresshe oil of roses. If ye will have this plaster
fair grene. than do therein the sap of night show (or solatri in latin) sap of
older / and celidonia of each. (...). (...) therewith let the salve sethe again
/ but not lunge / the longer it doth sethe the paler it ^eth / but the ^ethes
be not so wholesome / as the other be / nevertheless some masters doth this sap
therein / they know not what virtue power they have. the nyghshaw^ colyth and ^
doth ye (...) also / and celidonia clensyth / ^ore as ye put in this salve
much rosyll / so may ye the better this same sa^ do thereto / and. ii. or. iii.
ounces of (...) / than (...) it the more. Never can ^ome a good ^ without a mu^
/ for that ^ is ye key of the (...) and consolidatinu.

A good Jewes plaster to fresshe wounds.
Take why^. iiii. pound / raseno de (...) / that is whyt rosell / turpetyne of
each ii. pound / oil of roses one punde / mastik / (...) frankesence / myrra
of each. ii. ouces / fresh leues of roses. iiii. ouces / reed wine one mesure
of. iii. poude / of all these herbs take ye ie may get / winter grene or
pirola in latin / fyndowe / diapensia / waltmayster / or matrisylu^ in latin /
herba sarasenica / herba tuniri / herba solsiqui^ / betonica / cosolida minor /
sumus terre / platayne great and small / storks bill or herba rubea / in latin
/ valeriana / of each like much / till ye have enough / and good wine / till
ye have enough / stamp the herbs / and threst therout the sap / and put the
wine on the herbs yt they may be come well moysty with the wine / and let it
well sethe with the a foresaid wine / than steayne it thrugh a clothe / tha doth
sap and the wine in a kettyll / therein do the Way / Turpetyn / Rosyll / and
Oil than shall ye sethe the Roses with the rede wine till it give a blew flame
/ tha strain it thrugh a clothe / and do it also in the kettyll / and let it
sethe all together. v. or. vi. hours lunge / than take it from the fire / and
let it be cold / and the next day melt it again / and dother in the Mastyk /
Frank cence / and Myrre / made al in powder / and do in the kettyll / and let
it sethe together a walme or twain / and than take it of from the fire / and
let it be cold / than ye have a right iewes plaster that all wounds healed
without Tenttes.

Gracia dei.


GRacia dei like Master Peter de Ar^ set in the book (...) flesh making
medycyns. Take whyt Rosyl / whyt Wax / Armoniacu of each. xii. ounces /
Turpentyn. vi. ouces / Galbanu / ^banum / Mastyk / clear good wine / of each
anouc. Aristologia rotunda half an ouc. weke of this that is need to weke in
wine / therein is soden Betonica / Uerbina / Consolida mayor and minor / Sento
^a / Pinpinella / saint Johns herb or I^ricon / storks bill or herba rubea in
latin of each an handful / and al this parcels ye shall sethe in the wine /
till the wine be almost consiuned / and after make it with woman's milk as it
belongs / this plaster doth the flesh to grow and heleth / and it is come
for all wounds and fractures of the bones / and the surgyans that now be
praises it sore.

Attractinum.
Emplastrum attractinum / that is mudificatiuu / yt is to say / a drawing
plaster and it draws to him the matter / and all vnclennes of the
impostumation / vlceracion / sweryng of all vnclene woudes.

Take whyt rosyl a poude / maiden wax half a poude / hertes suet. viij. ouces
/ turpetyn. iiii. one. sarcocolle. si. ouces. mastyk whyt frakesece of each an
ou. myrra / aloe / succotrini of each half an ouc. melt yt wax rosyll / and
ye hertes luet rogyder / strain it thrugh a clothe / than do thereto the
turpetyne / and ye other parcels in powder / and oil of roses. ii. ounces /
styre this together till it be cold / will ye have this rede than do therein
iynopre in powder / if ye will have it ^yre yelow / than do therein a dragma
saffran in powder / if ye will have it grene so sethe sap of ye herbs therewith
/ thereof is said before in the grene plaster.

Adrawynge plaster.
A plaster that draws out arow hedes habergonnes maylles / and al that of
iron is / in the man body.

Take apostolicum Nicolai before said. ij ounces / magnete stone of wiete / that
hath his power half an ounce / hares grese / he^ see doyle of each half anoun^e
/ white dipt^ a dragma / melt that grefe and ye oil softly togider / and do
ye other parcels the tin^ that is made in powder / styre it together till it
be cold.

Another drawing plaster.
A plaster to take out thorns / splyntes^ glass / bones / and otherlyke things
/ that is in man body. Take diaquilon plaster out of this Antithodario. iij.
ounces magnete stone half an ounce / the rote of polipodiu / the rote of white
diptan / the rote of rethe (called i latin arudo) of each a drag ma and an half
/ hares grese anouc. and an hair / oil of hempseed an our. hereof make a
plaster as is before said.

A soft clensynge plaster.
A soft plaster that clensethal ^oulle wou des that is old / they that hath
roted flesh or makes much matter / and is called (...) dificatiuu de api^ /
this hath occupied (...) helmus / Lanc^ran^us / Hinricus de demon te villa.
Guido / all surgians of Paris.

Take sap of apium. ii. ounces / barley or wheete meele. iii. ounces / that shall
ye sethe with a soft fire till it bethy^ like a soft plaster / and as ye do
thereto sap of wormwode it let no fystyllcome in the wound / and ye wound
about fret not him self like the kancker or if the wound have ony^ than
shall ye do thereto sap of playntyne or sap of cr^sui^ / and ye do thereto farina
feny greci / or farina Iupinor^ / cures more stroger with dryngynge as
Theodoricu^ and Brunus saith.



The manner how ye shall make sum salves and oyntmentes very needful to the
surgeans.
AUreu vnguentu after the antithodario mesue / that all fresse wounds fylleth
with flesh / and helyth / Take yelowe wax xii. ouc. good oil of olyue a
pound and an halse / turpetyne iiij. ouces / greeks pytch / with rosyl / of
each v. ounces / white frankencence / mastyk of each. ii. ounces / saffran a
dragma / melt ye wax / oil / with the greeks pytch together and afterward do
therein turpentyn / and set it then from the fire / and make the other parselles
in powder / do this therein at ye half colynge / and styre it tha well till it be
cold.

Unguentum apostolorum.
Auicenna said vnguetum apostolorum clensyth a fystule / and makyth right good
/ and clensyth al corupt wounds of ye rotten flesh without payne / and
makyth that the flesh may grow.

A white Salve.
The white Salve after the Anthytodario Nicolay.
Take whyt lead. iiij. ouc. lytargiriu. ii. ouc. white frankincense. iij.
dragma. mastick. ii. dragma. each {per}sells make in powder by him self / and
mydle the white seed with a little oil / and do thereto litargirium /
thereafter mastick and frankincense / styre it with apesteyll of tentymes / and
at each time do therein a little rose water / when it begins to thycke put more
oil thereto and to each time a little rose water / and do it so lunge that it
be another to thycke nor to thynne.

Unguetn albu coferatum.
This white salve to make said Rasis.

Take oil olyue a pound and a half stamp white led a pound / white wax /
half a poude. campher. iii. dragma. iii. yol kes of eggs. this shall ye stamp
to gyder in a mortar / and in the lest do therein Campher in powder.

Unguentum Basylycon magnum.
This Salve set Mesue in his Antido thario / and is a great helper to the
wound there hete is in / and above all in the wounds of the synewes. and doth
cleanse and to grow flesh Take white rosyll / white wax / tallow of an ox
/ black pyt che / bird lyme / myrre / of each. iii. ounces. oil olyue that
there be Enough. thereof make a salve as thereto belongs.

Dyalthea.
This salve Dyalthea make after the Antithodario Nycolai.
Take hye malowe roots. ii. poude / lyn feed / fenygreke / of each a pound.
squille / half a pound. ye shall waste it well / than shall ye ye rotes /
lynseed / fenegreke / squille stamp / and lay it in. iii^. poude water. iii.
days lunge. and on the. iii^. day set it on ye fire and let it sede till it
begin to waxce thycke / and do it by little and little in a lyn nen bag /
and as ye will wrynge it out / and do thereto a little hot water yt the slyme
well may come out. and of the slyme take iii. poude. and do thereto oil olyue.
iiii. poude. than let it seed till the slyme consumes than do therein wax a
poude. and as that is melted do therein turpentyn galbanu / gumiedere / of each.
iii^. ouces. In the lest do therein greeks pytch or colofonie in latin / rosyll
And when it is wexed cold than do it lyghtely out.

Unguentum defensiuum and repercussiuuni.
This salve occupies comenly all masters to all wounds and bones / and
impostumacions / it restryngeth and defends ye no swerynge nor swellynge /
nor unpostume comes to the wounds or fractures of the bones / as the membre
be anointed therewith round about. Take rose oil. iii^. ounces. bolus armenus.
ii. ounces. terra sy gillata / (...) / of each an ounce. camfer a dragma.
nyghshawe or solatru in latyne howslyke / of each an handeful / and stamp it
and threst well out that sap / and mydle it to gyder cold like a white
salve.

Unguentum Egypciacum.
This Salve lerneth Galienus / Rasis / Albucasys / is sore occupies now in
this time of the surgeans / it cleanses softly and takeh away all vnclenes.

Take honey a poude. venegre half a poude. spanysshe grene. ii. ouc. alume one
ouc. this shall you sede all to gyder on ye fire till it be rede. And this
salve takes iii. manners of colours in his ^ethyng. If it is sod but a little
/ it seems grene. is it sod well tha it seems rede. is it soden to much /
than it seems black.

Unguentum fuscum.
This Salve doth flesh to grow / and ^lenseth and heleth. Take oil olyne
pound. iii^. ounces / wax. viii. ounces / greeks pytche / ship pytche / white
rosyll ofeche. iii^. ounces / mastycke / galbanum white frankincense /
turpentyne / myrra / ofeche. iii^. ounces / apoponatum / armonia cum / ofeche
an ounce / melt the oil and ye wax in a pane / and than put therein the
^yppytche and the greeks pytche / when it is molten strain it thrugh a cloth /
and stepe the gommes in vyneygre and soften them so / and strain it thrughe a
cloth and put it therein / and at the last put therein the other gommes in powder
/ and the turpentyne / and styre it together till it be cold.

Unguentu papuleon Nicolai.

This salve now a days the barbours makes contrary / and otherwise t^a^e it
should be / for sometime they put butter / sometime herbs that heleth / and they
lay the salve with lynte in the wound / and yt is contrary to the power of ye
popular salve for the nature of them is for to cole / and to take the payne
away / therefore it ought not to be made none otherwise then here after
following.

Take popular buds a pound and an half / hogs greece. iii^. pound stamp
them together / and let it stand till ye may have these herbs here after
following. Folia papaneris nigri / bramble leave of ye first buddynge / dolerote
leues / or folia de una versa / bylsem leues / or folia iusquiani / nyghshawe
leues / o^ folia solatri / folia de satyrion / muer pepper leues / or cras sula
in latin / letuse leues / violet leues / house leke / great bur leues / or
lapatium in latin / grounswell leues / of each. vi. ounces / and stamp these
herbs together with hogs greece / and with the buds of populen / let it
stand the space of. vii^ days / than put thereto wine. iii. pound than sethe
it in a kettle till the wine be sodden away / and than strain it thrugh a
cloth.

Oleum Nenufaris.
This oil is to the surgyans most profytable for it coleth the parsones / and
it must be made in like wise as the oil of camamyl is and in the stead of ^
take white see flowers / which herb has broad leues wymmynge upon the water
/ and it is called flores nenufarisin latin.

Oil of roses / without which oil no surgyan may be / and it must be made in
this manner as here after follows.

Take the sap of dust / or origani in latin / and water that roses be sodden
in / of each a pound / oleum sisamini washed / or take oil olyue the grenest
that ye can get. iii. pound / leues of roses a pound / and put them together
in a glass / and set it in the soon the space of. xiiii. days / than shall ye
sethe it in balneum marie till the sap and the water be consumed / and then
after ward strain it / and put therein again as much water of roses / and
sap as is before rehearsed / and set it again in the sonnr other. xiiii.
days / and than sethe it again in Balneum Marie as is before said / than
strain it and set it again in the ^onne and let it stand there the space
of. xl. days.

Oil of elder / or oil ofdygelet or any other oils made of flowers / they
must be made thus / as here after follows.

Take the flowers / or the herbs a pound / oil olyue. iii. pound / and put
it in a grass / set it in ye soon the spare of. xi. day* (...) / than ye shall
(...) the it in balneum marie and than strain it and threst it out / and the
oil of elder shall stand in the soon but iii. days / or else it will be
corrupt.



Here after follows a mance howe to make a drink for all wounds / and it is
needful for a surgyan.

A drink for all wounds and as a person is stricken thrughe the body / which
drink helps him inwardly with out powder / or other thing / nevertheless it is
good to lay on the wound a grene wounded plaster / for it cleanses ye wound
and this drink shall be made thus.

Take yue lea^s / or edera atbor^a growtynge on an oken we. iiii. dlmees /
winter grene smarta^d and gtete / or p^olam latin / fanycle or drapensia in
latin / syndau / herba for tis / or veronica / ofeche. ii. ounces / herba
solsqu^ an ounce / chop all these herbs small together and put them in a pewter
pot / and put thereto. iiii. pound and an half of the best wine / and a pound
and an half of water / and ye shall sethe them in balneum marie. iii. hours
lunge without taking of the lydde of the pot / then on the morrow after put
thereto. viii. ounces ofsuger / if the wound be in the heed / than put thereto
vy^onye. ii. ounces / sauge / an ounce / lafen dell half an ounce / and yfthe
wound be in the breast / than put thereto lycoresse. ii. ounces / polipodium an
ounce / ysope half an ounce / and yfthe pacy entteble sore / than put thereto
buglosse flowers / borage flowers oteche an ounce / roses / half an ounce /
than if the pacyent have great here put thereto violettes. ii. ounces / flores
uenuraris half an ounce / if ye wound be on ye lest side / than do thereto
liver wort an ounces matu^ua half an ounce / also if he have no going to the
draught / than it is be defull to put thereto seneleues / casse ^ of each. ij.
ounces / and if he be they wounded / than put thereto celidony votes. iiij.
ounces / and give it him to drink at morning / atnoone / and at evening / at
every time. iiij. ounces*

Another rostely drink for a wound.

Take winter grene / or^ / syndaw matrisilua / mufore / water evesses / or

Another costly drink for woudes in the heed / and also for all other wounds.

(...) the myddell pyll of the walte rote ^ in latin and scrape away ^ thereof

and morning / and at every time a sponefull and no more for the drink is
strong / and stepe a little clothe or a cole le^e in the drink and lay it on
the wound whether it be in the heed or in any other part or membre of the
body.

Here follows the correctyons of this presence book.
In the. xli. chapytre stands howe that yt the wound be in the syne w^s
beside the ceces that ye pacyent shall lose his life / but it is not so / for
it should be the pacyent shall lose his hearing and not his life.

Also in the same chapytre in the making o^plasters stands / frankincense /
mastye of each an ounce / and it should be of each a dragma.

Also ye shall find in the. xlv. chapytre in the glystres / violet leues /
herba mercurians of each an ouce / and it should be of each an handful.

Also in the same chapytre in the purgacyou should be pillule retidis maioris.

Also in the. xlvi^. chapytre in ye first powder should be the lyme of
eggeshelles.

Also in the. xlvii^. chapytre in the salve making stands florum camomille /
abscinthei / calamenti / salt rubbed of each. vii^. ounces it should be but.
iiii. ounces

Also in the. lxv. chapytre stands mastycke / gomine of araby: and thereby
should stand dragantum of each. ii. ounces.

Also in the. xcii. chapytre in the e^perte plastre stands white rosyll /
turpentyne black pytche / and there should be of each like much.

Also in the. xciii^. chapytre in the recepte in latin. Recipe specie cu
electuaru de gumis sieve species a dragma / specierium diadragantum frigidum.
i^. dragmas / and thereby should be diapenidiacu / manus xpi Also in the same
chapytre should stand in the syrupe of hearts tongue leues or scholopendre /
and there should be also borage flouces / plantayne / ofeche anounce.

Also in the. xcv. chapytre / in ye last salve and in the second paragraphe
for to consume the engyled blood / take venys soap cut small. iii^. ounces /
and there shall follow aqua vite. iij. ounces / vnguentu dyalthea. i^. ounces.

Also in Antithodario in vnguentu apostolorum is written / stepe this in vynegre
ii^. days lunge / as is galbanum armonia cum bdelliu / and thereby should
stand appoponatum. c.

Also in vnguentum dialthea is written turpentyne albanu / it should be galbanu
Also in the same dial the a stands in the end greeks pytche or colophonia in
latin rosyll / and thereby should stand of each a pound.

Also in vnguentum defenstuum is written terra sigillata / fenigreke / and that
fenegreke should be vynegre.

Also in ye third powder stands yrros and it should be yrees.

Also in the fourth powder stands spanysshe grene an ounce / and it should be
half an ounce.

Also in ye. vi^. powder stands flou^ and it should be flowers. Also in the ^
is ypoquiscidos / and it should be ypoquiscidos. Also in the same is nun^e for
(...).

Also in the. vii^. powder stands upon graves / and it should be upon deed
means heeds.

Also in the. ix. powder stands eyes of our lady / and it should be ye of
our rady it is like white asume.

Also in the second oil standetholeam / and it should be olium. Also in the
same is cestorie / and it should de castorie.

Also in the. iiii. drink stands ^ ^rum / and it should be cent^ in the same
is arthemusia for ^

Also in the. vi^. drink stands ^ and it should be pyrola. Also in ye ^
herba gross / it should he herb ^ few in english.

Also in ye. ix. drink stands ^ and it should be ambrosia.

Finis.
Thus ends the noble experience the bertuous handy work of Surgery / with
the Antithodario / practysed ^pyled by the expert master Iherome / which
book of late was translated out of the speech of hye Almayne into lowe Duche.
And afterward in to our mothers tongue of English / mochenecessary profytable
for surgyans / as well for the that have conynge / as for the that be lerners.
For who diligently often times redeth over this present book shall fyndether in
great science conynge. Imprinted at London in South warke by Petrus Creueris.
In the year of our lord god. M. D. xxv. and the. xxvi. day of Marche.
